祖父明白那个意思，是翠翠玩心与爱心相战争的结果。	The ferryman understood; she was at war with herself, torn between her own desire for fun and her love of him.
为了祖父的牵绊，应当玩的也无法去玩，这不成！	But it wouldn't do at all if she missed the fun that was her due just because she was tethered to him!
祖父含笑说：「翠翠，你这是为什么？说定了的又翻悔，同茶峒人平素品德不相称。我们应当说一是一，不许三心二意。	Grandpa said, with a smile, "Cuicui, what's wrong? Going back on your word is not what one expects of a Chadong girl. We stick to our promises, we don't give in to second thoughts.
我记性并不坏到这样子，把你答应了我的即刻忘掉」祖父虽那么说，很显然的事，祖父对于翠翠的打算是同意的。但人太乖了，祖父有点愀然不乐了。	My memory's not so bad that I forget your promises to me as soon as you make them!" So he said, but Grandpa obviously was prone to see things however she saw them. Yet because he doted on her, her change of heart saddened him, too.
见祖父不再说话，翠翠就说：「我走了，谁陪你？」	Seeing her grandpa fall silent, Cuicui asked him, "If I go, who will stay with you?"
祖父说：「你走了，船陪我。」	"If you go," he said, "the boat will stay with me!"
翠翠把眉毛皱拢去苦笑着，「船陪你，嗨，嗨，船陪你。爷爷，你真是－－」	Cuicui knitted her brows and gave him a wry smile: "Oh, so the boat will look after you. Is that right?"
祖父心想：「你总有一天会要走的。」	Grandpa thought to himself, "You will leave me, one day."
但不敢提这件事。祖父一时无话可说，于是走过屋后塔下小圃里去看葱，翠翠跟过去。	But he didn't dare bring that up. Grandpa didn't know what to say next, so he went out back of the house to the garden beneath the pagoda and checked on the scallions. Cuicui followed.
「爷爷，我决定不去，要去让船去，我替船陪你」	"Grandfather, I've made my decision. I'm not going. If someone has to go, let it be the boat. I'll take its place and keep you company!"
「好，翠翠，你不去我去，我还得戴了朵红花，装刘老老进城去见世面」	"Cuicui, if you won't go then I will, with red flowers in my hair, made up like an old country lady going to town on her first trip!"
两人都为这句话笑了许久。	The two of them laughed at this for the longest time. They left the dispute open to settlement.
祖父理葱，翠翠却摘了一根大葱呜呜吹着。	While Grandpa tended his scallions, Cuicui plucked a scallion with a big stem to use as a whistle.
有人在东岸喊过渡，翠翠不让祖父占先，便忙着跑下去，跳上了渡船，援着横溪缆子拉船过溪去接人。	People on the east bank called out to be ferried across.  Cuicui hurried over, blocking her grandpa's way.  She jumped into the boat and tugged it along the cable to the other side where the passengers were.
一面拉船一面喊祖父：	She yelled out to her grandpa:
「爷爷，你唱，你唱」	"Sing for us, Grandfather, sing!"
祖父不唱，却只站在高岩上望翠翠，把手摇着，一句话不说。	But he didn't. He just stood on the high crag, watching Cuicui and waving at her silently.
祖父有点心事。心事重重的，翠翠长大了。	Grandpa was a little worried.
翠翠一天比一天大了，无意中提到什么时会红脸了。	Cuicui was growing up, given to blushing now when certain things inadvertently came up in conversation.
时间在成长她，似乎正催促她，使她在另外一件事情上负点儿责。	The passage of time was ripening her, as if urging her forward, making her pay attention to new things.
她欢喜看扑粉满脸的新嫁娘，欢喜说到关于新嫁娘的故事，欢喜把野花戴到头上去，还欢喜听人唱歌。	She loved now to look at brides with their powder and makeup, to adorn her own hair with wildflowers, and to listen to songs.
茶峒人的歌声，缠绵处她已领略得出。	She was beginning to understand some of the sentiments in the local Chadong love songs.
她有时彷佛孤独了一点，爱坐在岩石上去，向天空一起云一颗星凝眸。	She seemed a little distant sometimes; she liked to sit on the rocky bluffs, fixing her gaze on a patch of clouds or a star in the sky.
祖父若问：「翠翠，想什么？」她便带着点儿害羞情绪，轻轻的说：「在看水鸭子打架」照当地习惯意思就是「翠翠不想什么」。但在心里却同时又自问：「翠翠，你真在想什么？」同是自己也在心里答着：「我想的很远，很多。可是我不知想些什么。」	Grandpa would ask, "Cuicui, what are you thinking about?" And she would whisper, embarrassed, "Cuicui's not thinking about anything." But at the same time she was asking herself, "Cuicui, what are you thinking about?" And she'd answer, "I'm thinking about lots of things, things that carry me far away. But I don't know what they are."
她的确在想，又的确连自己也不知在想些什么。这女孩子身体既发育得很完全，在本身上因年龄自然而来的一件「奇事」，到月就来，也使她多了些思索，多了些梦。	She was indeed wrapped up in thought, in thought that even she could not identify. Her girl's body had now completely filled out, and she had reached the age when she experienced a miracle of nature each month. This set her to thinking all the more.
祖父明白这类事情对于一个女子的影响，祖父心情也变了些。	Grandpa understood the impact of such things on a girl, and this in turn affected him.
祖父是一个在自然里活了七十年的人，但在人事上的自然现象，就有了些不能安排外。	He had lived his full seventy years amid nature, but some natural happenings in human life were beyond his control.
因为翠翠的长成，使祖父记起了些旧事，从掩埋在一大堆时间里的故事中，重新找回了些东西。	Cuicui's maturation made her grandpa recall events in the past.  From stories buried in the accumulations of time, certain things came back to haunt him.
翠翠的母亲，某一时节原同翠翠一个样子。眉毛长，眼睛大，皮肤红红的。	Cuicui's mother had once been just like her: long eyebrows, big eyes, rosy complexion, and a winsome charm that made you adore her.
也乖得使人怜爱－－也懂在一些小处，起眼动眉毛，使家中长辈快乐。	She was a clever one, knowing just how to roll her eyes and arch her eyebrows to the delight of family elders.
也彷佛永远不会同家中这一个分开。	One would have thought she, too, was incapable of leaving the old man.
但一点不幸来了，她认识了那个兵。	But then misfortune came: she met the soldier.
到末了丢开老的和小的，却陪那个兵死了。	In the end, she abandoned her elder and her young one to die with that soldier.
这些事从老船夫说来谁也无罪过，只应「天」去负责。	The old ferryman did not blame anyone for these things; he chalked it all up to Heaven.
翠翠的祖父口中不怨天，心却不能完全同意这种不幸的安排。	Cuicui's grandpa never cursed Heaven, but in his heart he could never completely accept its cruel disposition of things.
摊派到本身的一份，说来实在不公平！	He was still young at heart.
说是放下了，也正是不能放下的莫可奈何容忍到的一件事！	He said he had put it aside, yet it was something that couldn't be put aside, even though he must.
那时还有个翠翠。	And then there was Cuicui.
如今假若翠翠又同妈妈一样，老船夫的年龄，还能把小雏儿再育下去吗？	If Cuicui did as her mother did, could a man of his age bring up another baby?
人愿意神却不同意！	The gods would not necessarily consent, even if he were willing!
人太老了，应当休息了，凡是一个良善的乡下人，所应得到的劳苦与不幸，全得到了。	He was too old, ready for his rest.  All the toil and hardship that accompanied the life of a good and honest Chinese country fellow, he had already experienced.
假若另外高处有一个上帝，这上帝且有一双手支配一切，很明显的事，十分公道的办法，是应把祖父先收回去，再来让那个年青的在新的生活上得到应分接受那幸或不幸，才合道理。	If there really was a God up on high, and this God had two hands that could dispose of everything with perfect justice, He ought to take Grandpa first, letting the young people enjoy all that was due them in their new lives.
可是祖父并不那么想。	But Grandpa didn't think this way.
他为翠翠担心。	He was concerned about Cuicui.
他有时便躺到门外岩石上，对着星子想他的心事。	Sometimes he lay down on the bluffs under the stars to mull things over.
他以为死是应当快到了的，正因为翠翠人已长大了，证明自己也真正老了。	He felt that death would be coming for him soon.  The fact that Cuicui had grown up proved how old he was.
无论如何，得让翠翠有个着落。	Yet, whatever happened, he must get Cuicui settled.
翠翠既是她那可怜母亲交把他的，翠翠大了，他也得把翠翠交给一个人，他的事才算完结！	Cuicui's poor mother had given her to him.  Now that she had grown up, he must pass her on to someone else before his work on earth was done!
交给谁？	But who was the proper husband for her?
必需什么样的人方不委屈她？	Who could he be sure would never hurt her?
前几天顺顺家天保大老过溪时，同祖父谈话，这心直口快的青年人，第一句话就说：	A few days before, when the frank and outspoken Tianbao, Shunshun's No. 1, had crossed the stream and talked to Grandpa, the first words out of his mouth were:
「老伯伯，你翠翠长得真标致，像个观音样子。再过两年，若我有闲空能留在茶峒照料事情，不必像老鸦到处飞，我一定每夜到这溪边来为翠翠唱歌。」	"Elder Uncle, your Cuicui has grown quite beautiful. She's a real Guan Yin. Two years from now, if I can take charge of business in Chadong instead of having to fly over the landscape all day like a crow, I'll be coming by this stream every night to sing to Cuicui of my love."
祖父用微笑奖励这种自白。	Grandpa smiled to encourage him to go on with this declaration.
一面把船拉动，一面把那双小眼睛瞅着大老。	He looked at No. 1 with narrowed eyes while tugging the boat, as if to say, "I catch the meaning of your foolish confession, and it doesn't anger me. Go on  what else have you to say?"
于是大老又说：	Whereupon No. 1 continued:
「翠翠太娇了，我担心她只宜于听点茶峒人的歌声，不能作茶峒女子做媳妇的一切正经事。	"Cuicui is so delicate, I worry that she may be suited to listening to our Chadong love songs but not the humdrum errands of an ordinary Chadong wife.
我要个能听我唱歌的情人，却更不能缺少个照料家务的媳妇。	I want a sweetheart who can listen to my songs but she also has to be a wife who can manage household affairs.
『又要马儿不吃草，又要马儿走得好，』唉，这两句话恰是古人为我说的」	'I want a horse I don't have to feed, but I want it to run fast, too!'  The ancestors must have thought up that saying just for me, to show that you have to feed a horse to make it run fast!"
祖父慢条斯理把船掉了头，让船尾傍岸，就说：	Grandpa unhurriedly turned the boat around, putting the stern in to shore, and said:
「大老，也有这种事儿！你瞧着吧。」究竟是什么事，祖父可并不明白说下去。那青年走去后，祖父温习着那些出于一个男子口中的真话，实在又愁又喜。翠翠若应当交把一个人，这个人是不是适宜于照料翠翠？	"No. 1, anything can happen! Wait and see." After the young man left, Grandpa mulled over the boy's frank words. He was happy and at the same time worried.  Cuicui had to be entrusted to a husband.  Was this the best one to take care of her?
当真交把了他，翠翠是不是愿意？	And if he did bequeath her to him, would Cuicui be willing?
第八章	CHAPTER EIGHT
初五大清早落了点毛毛雨，上游且涨了点「龙船水」，河水全变作豆绿色。	A fine rain was falling at daybreak on the fifth of the month.
祖父上城买办过节的东西，戴了个粽粑叶「斗篷」，携带了一个篮子，一个装酒的大葫芦，肩头上挂了个褡裢，其中放了一吊六百钱，就走了。	Rising water levels upstream had provided the seasonal "Dragon Boat tide" and the river was already pea-green. Grandpa was on his way to town to buy goods for the festival, with a coolie hat made of phrynium fiber on his head and a bag containing a string of six hundred old imperial copper coins slung across his shoulder.  He carried a basket and a big gourd full of wine.
因为是节日，这一天从小村小寨带了铜钱担了货物上城去办货掉货的极多，这些人起身也极早，故祖父走后，黄狗就伴同翠翠守船。	Because it was a festival day, folk from all the little villages and Miao stockades had come bearing goods and money for buying, selling, and trading.  They had all arisen very early too, so Cuicui and the yellow dog tended the ferryboat in Grandpa's absence.
翠翠头上戴了一个崭新的斗篷，把过渡人一趟一趟的送来送去。	Cuicui wore a brand-new coolie hat as she ferried passengers back and forth, one trip after another.
黄狗坐在船头，每当船拢岸时必先跳上岸边去衔绳头，引起每个过渡人的兴味。	To the amusement of all, the yellow dog sat in the bow and, when they landed, jumped ashore before everyone else, carrying the tie rope in his mouth.
有些过渡乡下人也携了狗上城，照例如俗话说的，「狗离不得屋」，一离了自己的家，即或傍着主人，也变得非常老实了。	Some country folk brought their own dogs with them to town, but as the old saying goes, "dogs ought to be kept at home." Away from their territory, even accompanied by their masters, these dogs had to be on their best behavior.
到过渡时，翠翠的狗必走过去嗅嗅，从翠翠方面讨取了一个眼色，似乎明白翠翠的意思，就不敢有什么举动。	On the ferry, Cuicui's dog would go up and sniff at them until Cuicui threw him a cross look; he seemed to understand that she was telling him to stand back.
直到上岸后，把拉绳子的事情作完，眼见到那只陌生的狗上小山去了，也必跟着追去。	Even after landing, when he'd done his duty with the rope, he had to follow the unfamiliar dogs all the way up the hill.
或者向狗主人轻轻吠着，或者逐着那陌生的狗，必得翠翠带点儿嗔恼的嚷着：「狗，狗，你狂什么？还有事情做，你就跑呀！」于是这黄狗赶快跑回船上来，且依然满船闻嗅不已。翠翠说：「这算什么轻狂举动！跟谁学得的！还不好好蹲到那边去！」狗俨然极其懂事，便即刻到它自己原来地方去，只间或又像想起什么似的，轻轻的吠几声。	Whether he was barking softly at a dog's master or following the dog, Cuicui would yell at him, with a little anger in her voice: "Hey, there, dog! What's gotten into you? What makes you run off when we have work to do?" The yellow dog would quickly run back to the boat and go back to sniffing every place in sight. Cuicui said, "What nonsense is this? Where'd you learn that? Lie down over there!" As if he understood her words, the dog immediately went to his place in the boat and only occasionally gave a few soft yaps, as if he'd just remembered something.
雨落个不止，溪面一起烟。	The rain would not let up.  The river was covered with mist.
翠翠在船上无事可作时，便算着老船夫的行程。	When work quieted down on the boat, Cuicui rehearsed the old ferryman's itinerary in her imagination.
她知道他这一去应到什么地方碰到什么人，谈些什么话，这一天城门边应当是些什么情形，河街上应当是些什么情形，「心中一本册」，她完全如同眼见到的那么明明白白。她又知道祖父的脾气，一见城中相熟粮子上人物，不管是马夫火夫，总会把过节时应有的颂祝说出。	She knew just where he was going, whom he would run into and what they would say to each other, what would be going on at the city gate and on River Street  it was all in "the ledger of her mind," as clear as if she had seen it with her own eyes. And she knew her grandpa backward and forward. Every time he met an army friend from the city, even a horse groomer or a cook boy, he would give him the proper greetings of the day.
这边说，「副爷，你过节吃饱喝饱！」那一个便也将说，「划船的，你吃饱喝饱！」这边若说着如上的话，那边人说，「有什么可以吃饱喝饱？四两肉，两碗酒，既不会饱也不会醉！」那么，祖父必很诚实邀请这熟人过碧溪岨喝个够量。	He'd say, "Honorable Soldier, may you have your fill of good food and drink this holiday!" And the other would say, "Oarsman, may you have the same!" But if the reply to this salute was "What good food and drink do you mean? Four ounces of pork and two bowls of wine are not enough to satisfy anyone or get them drunk!," Grandpa would earnestly invite his friend to Green Creek Hill to drink up. If the man wanted to drink a swig of wine from Grandpa's gourd, the ferryman would not be tightfisted  he'd hand it right over.
倘若有人当时就想喝一口祖父葫芦中的酒，这老船夫也从不吝啬，必很快的就把葫芦递过去。酒喝过了，那兵营中人卷舌子舔着嘴唇，称赞酒好，于是又必被勒迫着喝第二口。	And if the man from the garrison rolled his tongue and licked his lips while praising the wine's quality, Grandpa would press him to take another swallow.
酒在这种情形下少起来了，就又跑到原来铺上去，加满为止。	Thus was the wine dissipated, until the ferryman ran back to the shop where he'd bought it to fill his gourd up to the top again.
翠翠且知道祖父还会到码头上去同刚拢岸一天两天的上水船水手谈谈话，问问下河的米价盐价，有时且弯着腰钻进那带有海带鱿鱼味，以及其他油味、醋味、柴烟味的船舱里去，水手们从小坛中抓出一把红枣，递给老船夫，过一阵，等到祖父回家被翠翠埋怨时，这红枣便成为祖父与翠翠和解的东西。	Cuicui knew, too, that Grandpa would go to the docks to talk to sailors whose boats had put in a day or two earlier.  He'd ask them the price of rice and salt downriver, and sometimes he'd stoop over and crawl into their cabins, which were steeped in the smells of squid and fish, sundry oils, vinegar, and smoke from the burning of wood.  The boatmen would grab a handful of red dates from a little jar and press them on the old ferryman. When Grandpa got home and heard Cuicui's complaints about his absence, these dates became the instruments of their reconciliation.
祖父一到河街上，且一定有许多铺子上商人送他粽子与其他东西，作为对这个忠于职守的划船人一点敬意，祖父虽嚷着「我带了那么一大堆，回去会把老骨头压断」，可是不管如何，这些东西多少总得领点情。	And when Grandpa got to River Street, many a shop owner would give him zongzi and other treats out of respect for this oarsman who was so true to his duty.  Though Grandpa would shout, "It'll crush my old bones to bring back a pile this big," he always had to give in to their gestures of gratitude.
走到卖肉案桌边去，他想「买肉」人家却不愿接钱，屠户若不接钱，他却宁可到另外一家去，决不想沾那点便宜。	He'd go to the long table where meat was sold and ask to buy, but they wouldn't take his money. If one butcher would refuse payment, he'd have to go to another rather than take advantage of others' goodwill.
那屠户说，「爷爷，你为人那么硬算什么？又不是要你去做犁口耕田！」但不行，他以为这是血钱，不比别的事情，你不收钱他会把钱预先算好，猛的把钱掷到大而长的钱筒里去，攫了肉就走去的。	The butcher would say, "Elder, why are you so unyielding about this? Nobody's asking you to be a beast of burden in front of the plow!" But he wouldn't take the offering. To him, this was akin to blood money, in a class of its own. If his money wasn't accepted, he'd figure out the meat's cost, thrust the coins into the bamboo tube that was the merchant's money box, seize the purchase, and leave.
卖肉的明白他那种性情，到他称肉时总选取最好的一处，且把份量故意加多，他见及时却将说：「喂喂，大老板，我不要你那些好处！腿上的肉是城里人炒鱿鱼肉丝用的肉，莫同我开玩笑！我要夹项肉，我要浓的糯的，我是个划船人，我要拿去炖葫萝卜喝酒的！」	The butcher, knowing how he would react beforehand, would give Grandpa the choicest portion and make sure it was overweight. But the ferryman might notice that and say, "Hey there, boss, I don't want any favors! Tenderloin cuts are for city people to saut   with squid. Don't make me laugh! I want meat from the neck, rich and sticky.  I row a boat. I want to make a stew of it with carrots while I drink my wine!"
得了肉，把钱交过手时，自己先数一次，又嘱咐屠户再数，屠户却照例不理会他，把一手钱哗的向长竹筒口丢去，他于是简直是妩媚的微笑着走了。	Meat in hand, he'd count out his payment before handing it over, then insist that the butcher count it again, but the latter would ignore this and throw the coins carelessly into his money tube.  The ferryman, as he left, would give a smile that had to be called ingratiating.
屠户与其他买肉人，见到他这种神气，必笑个不止－－	The butcher and his other customers found this hilarious.
翠翠还知道祖父必到河街上顺顺家里去。	Cuicui knew, too, that Grandpa would go to Shunshun's house on River Street.
翠翠温习着两次过节两个日子所见所闻的一切，心中很快乐，好像目前有一个东西，同早间在床上闭了眼睛所看到那种捉摸不定的黄葵花一样，这东西彷佛很明朗的在眼前，却看不准，抓不住。	She mused about everything she had seen and heard on the festival days of the past two years, joyful at heart, as if something had come to her, like the elusive yellow sunflower she saw with her eyes closed as she lay in bed in the morning. This thing loomed bright and bold before her, but she couldn't see it clearly or quite grasp it.
翠翠想：「白鸡关真出老虎吗？」她不知道为什么忽然想起白鸡关。白鸡关是酉水中部一个地名，离茶峒两百多里路！	Cuicui wondered: "Are there really tigers at White Rooster Pass?" She had no idea why she suddenly remembered White Rooster Pass. It was located in the middle reaches of the You River, over seventy miles from Chadong!
于是又想：「三十二个人摇六匹橹，上水走风时张起个大篷，一百幅白布铺成的一片东西，先在这样大船上过洞庭湖，多可笑－－」她不明白洞庭湖有多大，也就从没见过这种大船，更可笑的，还是她自己也不知道为什么却想到这个问题！	And then she thought: "Thirty-two men hefting six heavy oars, hoisting a great sail when the wind comes up, made from one hundred lengths of white cloth, crossing Lake Dongting in such a giant boat  how absurd!" She had no idea how big Lake Dongting was, nor had she ever seen such a big boat. Even funnier, she couldn't herself imagine why these thoughts had come to her.
一群过渡人来了，有担子，有送公事跑差模样的人物，另外还有母女二人。	A group arrived to be ferried across, people with goods: men who looked like government messengers and a mother and daughter.
母亲穿了新浆洗得硬朗的蓝布衣服，女孩子脸上涂着两饼红色，穿了不甚合身的新衣，上城到亲戚家中去拜节看龙船的。	The mother wore a blue outfit that had been starched stiff as a board and the girl's cheeks were rouged like two round cakes.  She wore new clothes that didn't fit too well.  They were going to town to greet their relatives at the festival and see the dragon boats.
等待众人上船稳定后，翠翠一面望着那小女孩，一面把船拉过溪去。	After waiting for the group to get settled on the boat, Cuicui gave the girl a once-over while she pulled the boat across the stream.
那小孩从翠翠估来年纪也将十三四岁了，神气却很娇，似乎从不曾离开过母亲。	To Cuicui, the girl looked to be about eleven and already very spoiled, always hanging on to her mother.
脚下穿的是一双尖头新油过的钉鞋，上面沾污了些黄泥。	Her newly polished shoes had pointy toes and spikes on the bottom, but they were splashed with mud.
裤子是那种泛紫的葱绿布做的。	Her trousers were made of leek-green cotton cloth with specks of purple.
见翠翠尽是望她，她也便看着翠翠，眼睛光光的如同两粒水晶球。	When she saw Cuicui staring at her, she stared back with eyes bright as crystal balls.
有点害羞，有点不自在，同时也有点不可言说的爱娇。	She looked a little embarrassed, ill at ease, and at the same time indefinably seductive.
那母亲模样的妇人便问翠翠年纪有几岁。	The mother then asked Cuicui how old she was.
翠翠笑着，不高兴答应，却反问小女孩今年几岁。	Cuicui smiled, unwilling to answer, and instead asked how old her daughter was.
听那母亲说十三岁时，翠翠忍不住笑了。	When she said twelve years old, Cuicui couldn't suppress a laugh.
那母女显然是财主人家的妻女，从神气上就可看出的。	They were obviously the wife and daughter of a rich man; one could tell from their manner.
翠翠注视那女孩，发现了女孩子手上还戴得有一副麻花绞的银手镯，闪着白白的亮光，心中有点儿歆羡。	Cuicui spotted a pair of bracelets on the girl, made of interlaced strands of silver.  They flashed a shiny white light and made Cuicui feel a little envious.
船傍岸后，人陆续上了岸，妇人从身上摸出一铜子，塞到翠翠手中，就走了。	When the boat reached shore and everyone was off, the woman took out a copper coin and pressed it into Cuicui's hand before going.
翠翠当时竟忘了祖父的规矩了，也不说道谢，也不把钱退还，只望着这一行人中那个女孩子身后发痴。	Forgetting her grandpa's rule for the moment, Cuicui neither thanked her nor gave it back.  She just gaped from behind at the girl among the file of people.
一行人正将翻过小山时，翠翠忽又忙匆匆的追上去，在山头上把钱还给那妇人。	The group was about to go up the hill when Cuicui suddenly chased after them.
那妇人说：「这是送你的！」翠翠不说什么，只微笑把头尽摇，且不等妇人来得及说第二句话，就很快的向自己渡船边跑去了。	At the top of the hill, she returned the money to the woman, who said, "It's for you!" Cuicui just smiled and shook her head without replying, to indicate that she couldn't accept it, and without waiting for the woman to say another word, she quickly ran back to her ferryboat.
到了渡船上，溪那边又有人喊过渡，翠翠把船又拉回去。	When she reached the boat, people on the opposite shore were summoning the ferry, so Cuicui tugged the boat across.
第二次过渡是七个人，又有两个女孩子，也同样因为看龙船特意换了干净衣服，相貌却并不如何美观，因此使翠翠更不能忘记先前那一个。	Seven people crossed on this trip, among them two more girls, who also wore clean outfits to go see the boat races.  But they were not so attractive; this made Cuicui fix her mind all the more on the previous girl.
今天过渡的人特别多，其中女孩子比平时更多，翠翠既在船上拉缆子摆渡，故见到什么好看的，极古怪的，人乖的，眼睛眶子红红的，莫不在记忆中留下个印象。	More people than usual needed ferrying today, especially girls.  Cuicui pulled them across on the boat, so they made a deep impression on her: the pretty ones, the funny-looking ones, the nice ones, ones with reddened eyes.
无人过渡时，等着祖父祖父又不来，便尽只反复温习这些女孩子的神气。且轻轻的无所谓的唱着：	When the crowds stopped, while she waited for Grandpa and Grandpa didn't come, she reviewed all of the girls in her mind and sang softly and distractedly:
「白鸡关出老虎咬人，不咬别人，团总的小姐派第一。	The tiger at White Rooster Pass feasts on people And he' ll get the militia captain's daughter first.
－－大姐戴副金簪子，二姐戴副银钏子，只有我三妹没得什么戴，耳朵上长年戴条豆芽菜。」	Sister No. 1 wears a pair of gold hairpins, Sister No. 2, a pair of silver bracelets, But Sister No. 3, little me, has no jewelry to be found; Just bean-sprout earrings, worn all the year round.
城中有人下乡的，在河街上一个酒店前面，曾见及那个撑渡船的老头子，把葫芦嘴推让给一个年青水手，请水手喝他新买的白烧酒，翠翠问及时，那城中人就告给她所见到的事情。	A man came from town who'd seen the old ferryman in front of a tavern on River Street, offering a young boatman his gourd full of freshly bought white liquor.  Cuicui inquired further and he told all.
翠翠笑祖父的慷慨不是时候，不是地方。	She laughed to hear of her grandpa's generosity, offered at just the wrong time and the wrong place.
过渡人走了，翠翠就在船上又轻轻的哼着巫师十二月里为人还愿迎神的歌玩－－	As the man departed, Cuicui again began to softly hum, just for fun, the chant that the local shaman used to summon the gods:
你大仙，你大神，睁眼看看我们这里人！	Gods and immortals, open your eyes and look at us down here!
他们既诚实，又年青，又身无疾病。	Our young are honest and healthy.
他们大人会喝酒，会作事，会睡觉；他们孩子能长大，能耐饥，能耐冷；他们牯牛肯耕田，山羊肯生仔，鸡鸭肯孵卵；他们女人会养儿子，会唱歌，会找她心中欢喜的情人！	Our elders know how to drink, and work, and sleep; Our children grow up to withstand hunger and cold; Our oxen are willing to plow, our sheep to birth, our fowl to hatch eggs; Our women are good at raising children, singing, and finding their true loves!
你大神，你大仙，排驾前来站两边。	Gods and immortals, come on down and have a look.
关夫子身跨赤兔马，尉迟公手拿大铁鞭！	Lord Guan, mount the Red-haired Steed, General Weichi Gong, brandish the iron whip.
你大仙，你大神，云端下降慢慢行！	Gods and immortals above, ride down on the clouds and look around!
张果老驴得坐稳，铁拐李脚下要小心！	Old Man Zhang Guo, ride steady on your donkey, Iron Crutch Li, be careful where you step!
福禄绵绵是神恩，和风和雨神好心，好酒好饭当前阵，肥猪肥羊火上烹！	Riches and emoluments without end come from the gods; Timely winds and rains, too, come from your favor, So good wine and food are laid before you, Fat pigs and sheep are frying in the pan.
洪秀全，李鸿章，你们在生是霸王，杀人放火尽节全忠各有道，今来坐席又何妨！	Hong Xiuquan, Li Hongzhang, Once you were lords of all around, Murder and arson  suicide and loyalty  each has its art, So join the feast, it's for you to take part.
慢慢吃，慢慢喝，月白风清好过河。	Eat and drink, please take your time, Moon's up and breeze's down; fording the river will be just fine.
醉时携手同归去，我当为你再唱歌！	If you're drunk I'll take your hand and lead you along, So I can treat you to another song.
那首歌声音既极柔和，快乐中又微带忧郁。	The melody was very sweet, full of happiness tinged with melancholy.
唱完了这歌，翠翠觉得心上有一丝儿凄凉。	When she finished singing it, Cuicui felt a little despondent.
她想起秋末酬神还愿时田其中的火燎同鼓角。	She recalled the prairie fires and drumbeats at the end of autumn when it was time for rewarding the gods and redeeming promises to them.
远处鼓声已起来了，她知道绘有朱红长线的龙船这时节已下河了，细雨还依然落个不止，溪面一起烟。	The drumbeats from afar had already begun to sound. She knew that this must mark the dragon boats, painted with their vermilion stripes, going into the river. It was still drizzling endlessly and a layer of mist hung over the creek.
第九章	CHAPTER NINE
祖父回家时，大约已将近平常吃早饭时节了，肩上手上全是东西，一上小山头便喊翠翠，要翠翠拉船过小溪来迎接他。	When Grandpa got home, it was almost time for breakfast.  Arms and shoulder poles laden with packages, he called out for Cuicui from the top of the hill for her to pull the boat across the stream to meet him.
翠翠眼看到多少人皆进了城，正在船上急得莫可奈何，听到祖父的声音，精神旺了，锐声答着：「爷爷，爷爷，我来了」老船夫从码头边上了渡船后，把肩上手上的东西搁到船头上，一面帮着翠翠拉船，一面向翠翠笑着，如同一个小孩子，神气充满了谦虚与羞怯。	Having seen so many people getting to go to town, Cuicui there in the boat was beside herself with impatience, but the sound of her grandpa picked up her spirits.  She hollered back, shrilly, "Grandfather, Grandfather, I'm coming!" When the old ferryman had got into the boat and set down his load in the prow, he helped tug the boat as he smiled at Cuicui, himself as meek and bashful as a child.
「翠翠，你急坏了，是不是？」翠翠本应埋怨祖父的，但她却回答说：「爷爷，我知道你在河街上劝人喝酒，好玩得很。」翠翠还知道祖父极高兴到河街上去玩，但如此说来，将更使祖父害羞乱嚷了，因此话到口边却不提出。	"Cuicui, I'll bet you thought I was never coming, didn't you?" She was going to complain to her grandpa, but instead she answered, "Grandfather, I knew you were on River Street, plying people with wine, having a wonderful time." Cuicui knew how much her grandpa loved to hang around on River Street, but to go on about it would have made her grandpa sputter embarrassed denials, so she kept it back.
翠翠把搁在船头的东西一一估记在眼里，不见了酒葫芦。	Counting up all the bundles in the prow, Cuicui noticed that the wine gourd was missing.
翠翠嗤的笑了。	She snickered.
「爷爷，你倒大方，请副爷同船上人吃酒，连葫芦也吃到肚里去了」	"Grandfather, you're so generous, letting all those soldiers and boatmen drink off you, you even let them swallow your gourd!"
祖父笑着忙作说明：	Smiling, Grandpa quickly put in:
「哪里，哪里，我那葫芦被顺顺大伯扣下了，他见我在河街上请人喝酒，就说：『喂，喂，摆渡的张横，这不成的。	"No way, no way. Elder Brother Shunshun took it away from me. He saw me out on River Street inviting people to have a drink and said, 'Hey there, Captain Zhang Heng of the ferrymen, we can't have this.
你不开槽坊，如何这样子！	You don't own a distillery!  How can you go on like this?
把你那个放下来，请我全喝了吧。	If you have to be a philanthropist, a real sport like the heroes of Mount Liang, then give it over, I'll drink it up for you!'
』他当真那么说，『请我全喝了吧。	That's what he said, 'I'll drink it up for you!'
』我把葫芦放下了。	I put down my wine gourd.
但我猜想他是同我闹着玩的。	But I figure he was kidding me.
他家里还少烧酒吗？	Is there any lack of wine in his household?
翠翠，你说，－－」	What do you think, Cuicui?"
「爷爷，你以为人家真想喝你的酒，便是同你开玩笑吗？」	"Grandfather, do you really think it was about him having a drink, even if it was all in jest?"
「那是怎么的？」	"What, then?"
「你放心，人家一定因为你请客不是地方，所以扣下你的葫芦，不让你请人把酒喝完。等等就会为你送来的，你还不明白，真是！－－」	"Nothing to be upset over, he must have confiscated your gourd because you picked the wrong place to be serving all comers; he didn't want you to end up with no liquor at all. He'll send it back with one of his men in a little while.  You still don't get it! For Heaven's sake!"
「唉，当真会是这样的」	"Do you really think he will?"
说着船已拢了岸，翠翠抢先帮祖父搬东西，但结果却只拿了那尾鱼，那个花褡裢；褡裢中钱已用光了，却有一包白糖，一包小芝麻饼子。	By this time the boat had reached the shore.  Cuicui hurried to help her grandpa gather up his bundles before he could pick them up, but all she got was a lone fish and the embroidered waist pouch.  The money was already gone; in its place were a packet of white sugar and a box of sesame cakes.
两人刚把新买的东西搬运到家中，对溪就有人喊过渡，祖父要翠翠看着肉菜免得被野猫拖去，争着下溪去做事，一会儿，便同那个过渡人嚷着到家中来了。	The two had just brought the new purchases into the house when someone hailed them for service from the other side of the stream.  Asking Cuicui to keep an eye on the meat and vegetables lest a feral cat get them, Grandpa rushed ahead of her to the ferry.  After a short time, he headed back home with the passenger, speaking loudly and excitedly.
原来这人便是送酒葫芦的。只听到祖父说：「翠翠，你猜对了。人家当真把酒葫芦送来了」	The visitor had indeed come to return the gourd. Grandpa said, "Cuicui, you guessed right! He really did bring it back!"
翠翠来不及向灶边走去，祖父同一个年纪青青的脸黑肩膊宽的人物，便进到屋里了。	Before Cuicui could escape into the kitchen, Grandpa entered the house with a young man. He was dark and broad-shouldered.
翠翠同客人皆笑着，让祖父把话说下去。	Cuicui and the visitor smiled at each other, letting Grandpa talk on.
客人又望着翠翠笑，翠翠彷佛明白为么被人望着，有点不好意思起来，走到灶边烧火去了。	The guest kept on looking and smiling at Cuicui, who seemed to realize what the staring meant.  She began to grow a little embarrassed, so she went into the kitchen to light the fire in the stove.
溪边又有人喊过渡，翠翠赶忙跑出门外船上去，把人渡过了溪。	When yet another person came to the stream and hailed the ferry, she ran out the door to the boat and took him across.
恰好又有人过溪。	And just then there was another passenger.
天虽落小雨，过渡人却分外多，一连三次。	Though it was drizzling, there were far more people to serve than usual, requiring three trips.
翠翠在船上一面作事一面想起祖父的趣处。	Once on board, as Cuicui tended the boat, she began thinking about her granddad's happy mood.
不知怎么的，从城里被人打发来送酒葫芦的，她觉得好像是个熟人。	She sensed, somehow, that she knew this city fellow who'd been dispatched to return the wine gourd.
可是眼睛里像是熟人，却不明白在什么地方见过面。	But though he looked familiar, she didn't know where she'd seen him before.
但也正像是不肯把这人想到某方面去，方猜不着这来人的身分。	She seemed unwilling to figure it all out and could not guess his identity.
祖父在岩坎上边喊：「翠翠，翠翠，你上来歇歇，陪陪客」本来无人过渡便想上岸去烧火，但经祖父一喊，反而不上岸了。	Grandpa hollered from the bluff: "Cuicui! Cuicui! Come up and sit awhile, keep our guest company!" She'd intended to go ashore and light the stove since no one needed ferrying, but now that her grandpa had called her, she didn't.
来客问祖父「进不进城看船」，老渡船夫就说「应当看守渡船」。两人又谈了些别的话。到后来客方言归正传：	The visitor asked Grandpa, "Are you going to town to see the boats?" "I have to stay with my boat," replied the old ferryman. The two continued talking about other things. Finally, the visitor came to the point:
「伯伯，你翠翠像个大人了，长得很好看」	"Uncle, your Cuicui is grown up now. She's very pretty!"
撑渡船的笑了。「口气同哥哥一样，倒爽快呢。」这样想着，却那么说：「二老，这地方配受人称赞的只有你，人家都说你好看：八面山的豹子，地地溪的锦鸡，』全是特为颂扬你这个人好处的警句」	The ferryman smiled. "He talks just like his elder brother  says exactly what's on his mind," he thought to himself. But he said, "No. 2, you're the only one in these parts who deserves that praise. Everybody says you're handsome! Folks have made up epithets to acclaim your virtues: the Leopard of Bamian Mountain, the Golden Pheasant of Didi Stream!"
「但是，这很不公平。」	"What nonsense!"
「很公平的！我听船上人说，你上次押船，船到三门下面白鸡关滩出了事，从急浪中你援救过三个人。你们在滩上过夜，被村子里女人见着了，人家在你棚子边唱歌一整夜，是不是真有其事？」	"They've really captured you! I heard some boatmen say that last time when you were piloting a boat and it wrecked up below the Three Gorges in the rapids at White Rooster Pass, you rescued three men from the dashing waves. They say you stayed overnight by the rapids, and when the village girls got a look at you, they crooned the night away with love songs outside your shack. Is it true?"
「不是女人唱歌一夜，是狼嗥。那地方著名多狼，只想得机会吃我们！	"That wasn't any serenading by young women, that was the howling of wolves! The place is famous for them, just looking for the chance to eat us!
我们烧了一大堆火，吓住了它们，才不被吃掉」	We kept a big campfire to scare them off  that's the only way we escaped with our lives!"
老船夫笑了，「那更妙！人家说的话还是很对的。狼是只吃姑娘，吃小孩，吃十八岁标致青年，像我这种老骨头，它不要吃的」	The old ferryman chuckled: "All the more! What they said about you was right! A wolf only picks out young maidens and children to eat  and handsome young seventeen-year-olds  never an old bones like me. It'd take one sniff at me and go away!"
那二老说：「伯伯，你到这里见过两万个日头，别人家全说我们这个地方风水好，出大人，不知为什么原因，如今还不出大人？」	At that, No. 2 said, "Uncle, you've seen a lot of sunrises in this locale. Everybody says the excellent feng shui here, the geomancy, is propitious for the emergence of great men. I wonder why we haven't had one so far?"
「你是不是说风水好应出有大名头的人？我以为这种人不生在我们这个小地方，也不碍事。	"You mean the good feng shui should have given us someone with a big name? I don't see anything so bad about not having such a person born in a little place like this.
我们有聪明，正直，勇敢，耐劳的年青人，就够了。	It's enough that we have young people who are bright, honest, brave, and able to work hard.
像你们父子兄弟，为本地也增光彩已经很多很多」	The men in your family, for instance, have brought this place a lot of glory!"
「伯伯，你说得好，我也是那么想。地方不出坏人出好人，如伯伯那么样子，人虽老了，还硬朗得同棵楠木树一样，稳稳当当的活到这块地面，又正经，又大方，难得的咧。」	"Uncle, you're right, I was just thinking that. This place of ours produces good men, not bad men  men like you, Uncle. You may be old, but you're still as strong as a nanmu tree, living a steady and stable life on this patch of earth  both decent and generous. There aren't many like you."
「我是老骨头了，还说什么。日头，雨水，走长路，挑份量沉重的担子，大吃大喝，挨饿受寒，自己分上的都拿过了，不久就会躺到这冰凉土地上喂蛆吃的。这世界有得是你们小伙子分上的一切，好好的干，日头不辜负你们，你们也莫辜负日头」	"I'm an old man, what am I worth? I've had everything that was my lot in life: sun and rain, long journeys bearing heavy loads, living it up on food and liquor, then suffering hunger and cold  and pretty soon, I'll be lying beneath the cold, cold earth, feeding the earthworms. There's plenty waiting on this earth for you young folk. If you do your work well, it won't let you down  just hold up your end of the bargain."
「伯伯，看你那么勤快，我们年青人不敢辜负日头」	"Uncle, with your diligence setting the example, we young people dare not let you down!"
说了一阵，二老想走了，老船夫便站到门口去喊叫翠翠，要她到屋里来烧水煮饭，掉换他自己看船。	They'd been talking for some time, so No. 2 was ready to go.  The old ferryman stood outside his doorway and called for Cuicui to come into the house to boil water and cook a meal while he took her place on the boat.
翠翠不肯上岸，客人却已下船了，翠翠把船拉动时，祖父故意装作埋怨神气说：	Cuicui didn't want to come ashore, but the guest had already boarded the boat, so as she tugged the boat, Grandpa pretended to scold her:
「翠翠，你不上来，难道要我在家里做媳妇煮饭吗？」	"Cuicui, aren't you coming back? Surely you don't expect me to be a housewife and do the cooking?"
翠翠斜睨了客人一眼，见客人正盯着她，便把脸背过去，抿着嘴儿，很自负的拉着那条横缆，船慢慢拉过对岸了。	Throwing a sidelong glance at the visitor, Cuicui saw that he was staring at her.  Turning her head away and pursing her lips, she smartly attended to her business pulling on the cable, until she'd slowly pulled the boat onto the shore.
客人站在船头同翠翠说话：	The visitor stood in the prow and said to Cuicui,
「翠翠，吃了饭，同你爷爷去看划船吧？」	"Cuicui, when you've eaten, won't you come with your grandfather to our stilt house and watch the boat race?"
翠翠不好意思不说话，便说：「爷爷说不去，去了无人守这个船」	At first too embarrassed to speak, Cuicui finally answered, "Grandfather says he's not going, because then there'd be no one to tend the ferry!"
「你呢？」	"Won't you come?"
「爷爷不去我也不去。」	"If Grandfather won't go, neither will I."
「你也守船吗？」	"Do you have to tend the boat, too?"
「我陪我爷爷。」	"I want to be with Grandfather."
「我要一个人来替你们守渡船，好不好？」	"What if I get someone to take your place on the boat?"
砰的一下船头已撞到岸边土坎上了，船拢岸了。	The boat reached the shore with a thud as it bumped into a mound of earth.
二老向岸上一跃，站在斜坡上说：	No. 2 jumped up on the bank and said, from the slope:
「翠翠，难为你！－－我回去就要人来替你们，你们快吃饭，一同到我家里去看船，今天人多咧，热闹咧」	"Cuicui, I've put you to trouble. When I get home, I'll send someone to take the place of both of you. Eat your meal and hurry on over to my house to see the boats.  A lot of people are there already, it's very lively!"
翠翠不明白这陌生人的好意，不懂得为什么一定要到他家中去看船，抿着小嘴笑笑，就把船拉回去了。	Misunderstanding the good intentions of this stranger, and why she had to go to his house to see the boats, Cuicui giggled between her little pursed lips and pulled the boat back to the other shore.
到了家中一边溪岸后，只见那个人还正在对溪小山上，好像等待什么，不即走开。	When she got to the bank where her home was, the young man had reached the top of the hill on the other side.  He was still there, as if waiting for something.
翠翠回转家中，到灶口边去烧火，一面把带点湿气的草塞进灶里去，一面向正在把客人带回的那一葫芦酒试着的祖父询问：	Cuicui went home and lit the fire.  She stuffed some damp grasses into the stove and inquired of her grandpa, who was just then testing out the wine in the gourd returned by the visitor.
「爷爷，那人说回去就要人来替你，要我们两人去看船，你去不去？」	"Grandfather, that fellow said he was going back to get someone to replace you, so the two of us can go see the races. Will you go?"
「你高兴去吗？」	"Would you like to?"
「两人同去我高兴。那个人很好，我像认得他，他是谁？」	"If we go together. I like that young man. He seems familiar. Who is he?"
祖父心想：「这倒对了，人家也觉得你好」祖父笑着说：	"Good, he likes you, too!" Grandpa thought to himself. He said, with a smile,
「翠翠，你不记得你前年在大河边时，有个人说要让大鱼咬你吗？」	"Cuicui, don't you remember two years ago, you were on the big riverbank and someone said you might be eaten by a big fish?"
翠翠明白了，却仍然装不明白问：「他是谁？」	Cuicui understood, but she pretended not to. She asked, "Who is he, then?"
「你想想看，猜猜看。」	"Think, Cuicui. Take a guess."
「一本《百家姓》好多人，我猜不着他是张三李四。」	"I couldn't possibly guess who he is."
「顺顺船总家的二老，他认识你你不认识他啊」他抿了一口酒，像赞美酒又像赞美人，低低的说：「好的，妙的，这是难得的。」	"He's No. 2 of Fleetmaster Shunshun's household. He remembered you, but you still don't remember him!" He took a sip of wine and said, in a low voice, as if to praise the wine and a certain man at the same time: "Good, just right. You're not this lucky very often!"
过渡的人在门外坎下叫唤着，老祖父口中还是「好的，妙的－－」匆匆下船做事去了。	People wanting the ferry hailed him from outside the door. The old grandpa reiterated, "Good, just right  " Then in a flash he was in the boat, getting down to work.
第十章	CHAPTER TEN
吃饭时隔溪有人喊过渡，翠翠抢着下船，到了那边，方知道原来过渡的人，便是船总顺顺家派来作替手的水手，一见翠翠就说道：「二老要你们一吃了饭就去，他已下河了。	While they were eating, someone called for the ferry on the far bank.  Cuicui rushed to the boat.  When she got to the other shore, she saw that her passenger was the boatman sent by Fleetmaster Shunshun to take their place.
」见了祖父又说：「二老要你们吃了饭就去，他已下河了。」	He looked at Cuicui and said, "No. 2 wants you to come over when you finish eating. He's already in his dragon boat." He said the same thing when he saw Grandpa.
张耳听听，便可听出远处鼓声已较密，从鼓声里使人想到那些极狭的船，在长潭中笔直前进时，水面上画着如何美丽的长长的线路！	Straining their ears, they could hear the faraway drumbeats picking up their pace, and from that they could picture the very slender boats dashing straight ahead across the Long Depths, their wakes leaving long and exquisitely beautiful lines in the water.
新来的人茶也不吃，便在船头站妥了，翠翠同祖父吃饭时，邀他喝一杯，只是摇头推辞。	Unwilling even to stop for tea, the newcomer took a position in the prow of the boat.  Cuicui and Grandpa had invited him in during their meal, but he shook his head.
祖父说：	Grandpa said,
「翠翠，我不去，你同小狗去好不好？」	"Cuicui, I'm not going, why don't you and the little dog go on without me?"
「要不去，我也不想去！」	"If you don't go, I don't want to, either!"
「我去呢？」	"And if I do?"
「我本来也不想去，但我愿意陪你去。」	"I didn't really want to, but I'd go with you."
祖父微笑着，「翠翠，翠翠，你陪我去，好的，你陪我去！」	Grandpa smiled: "All right, Cuicui, you come with me, keep me company!"
祖父同翠翠到城里大河边时河边早站满了人。	By the time Grandpa and Cuicui got to the big river in the city, the banks had been crowded with spectators for some time.
细雨已经停止，地面还是湿湿的。	The drizzle had stopped, but the ground was still wet.
祖父要翠翠过河街船总家吊脚楼上去看船，翠翠却以为站在河边较好。	Grandpa wanted Cuicui to go to the fleetmaster's stilt house on River Street to watch the races, but something seemed to be weighing on her mind that made her afraid to go there; she preferred to stand by the riverbank.
两人在河边站定不多久，顺顺便派人把他们请去了。	Though the two stayed in place there, it wasn't long before Shunshun sent someone to invite them in.
吊脚楼上已有了很多的人。	His house on stilts was already crowded.
早上过渡时，为翠翠所注意的乡绅妻女，受顺顺家的款待，占据了最好窗口，一见到翠翠，那女孩子就说：「你来，你来！」	The upper-class country mother and daughter that had caught Cuicui's eye when she ferried them that morning occupied the two best seats in the house, by the window. The daughter spotted Cuicui and said: "Come here, over here!"
翠翠带着点儿羞怯走去，坐在他们身后条凳上，祖父便走开了。	Cuicui went over, a little self-consciously, and sat on a bench behind them. Grandpa set off.
祖父并不看龙船竞渡，却为一个熟人拉到河上游半里路远近，到一个新碾坊看水碾子去了。	Instead of watching the dragon boats race, Grandpa let an acquaintance lead him away to see the new grain mill and its water-powered stone roller a quarter-mile upstream.
老船夫对于水碾子原来就极有兴味的。	The old ferryman happened to be intensely interested in that mill.
倚山滨水来一座小小茅屋，屋中有那么一个圆石片子，固定在一个横轴上，斜斜的搁在石槽里。	In a tiny thatched hut nestled between the mountain and the river was the round millstone, fixed vertically on a horizontal axle and resting at a tilt on top of a circular pathway of crushed stone along which it would make its revolutions.
当水闸门抽去时，流水冲激地下的暗轮，上面的石片便飞转起来。	When the sluice gate was pulled up, water rushed down upon a concealed underground wheel, and the round millstone up above flew into action, rotating on its axle as it made its rounds over the circular pathway under it.
作主人的管理这个东西，把毛谷倒进石槽中去，把碾好的米弄出放在屋角隅筛子里，再筛去糠灰。	The miller poured his unhusked rice into the groove of the stone circuit on the bottom.  When the polished rice came out, he sifted away the powdery chaff in a rectangular bamboo sieve basket he kept in the corner of the hut.
地上全是糠灰，主人头上包着块白布帕子，头上肩上也全是糠灰。	The floor was covered in this dust from the chaff, and so were the miller's head and shoulders, from top to bottom, including the white cloth he wrapped around his head like a turban.
天气好时就在碾坊前后隙地里种些萝卜、青菜、大蒜、四季葱。	In good weather he went out to the open spaces around the millhouse, where he planted turnips, cabbages, garlic, and scallions.
水沟坏了，就把裤子脱去，到河里去堆砌石头修理泄水处。	When the millrace got damaged, he took off his trousers and went into the river to pile up rocks so as to plug the leak.
水碾坝若修筑得好，还可装个小小鱼梁，涨小水时就自会有鱼上梁来，不劳而获！	Once his dikes were firmly built, he could build a net of branches across the millrace, like a bridge.  When the waters rose, fish would swim right over the dike into it, without the miller's having to lift a finger!
在河边管理一个碾坊比管理一只渡船多变化有趣味，情形一看也就明白了。	Compared to running a ferry, running a mill was a more multifaceted and interesting job; that was clear at a glance.
但一个撑渡船的若想有座碾坊，那简直是不可能的妄想。	But it was wholly in vain for a ferryman to hope to have a mill someday.
凡碾坊照例是属于当地小财主的产业。	Mills all belonged to the local rich people.
那熟人把老船夫带到碾坊边时，就告给他这碾坊业主为谁。	The old ferryman's friend told him who the mill's owner was.
两人一面各处视察一面说话。	The two men looked over every corner of it as they chatted.
那熟人用脚踢着新碾盘说：	The ferryman's friend kicked the new millstone and said:
「中寨人自己坐在高山砦子上，却欢喜来到这大河边置产业；这是中寨王团总的，大钱七百吊！」	"The people of Middle Stockade live up high in the mountains, but they like to buy property down here by the river; this mill belongs to Middle Stockade's Militia Captain Wang. Cost him seven hundred strings of cash, a thousand coppers to a string!"
老船夫转着那双小眼睛，很羡慕的去欣赏一切，估计一切，把头点着，且对于碾坊中对象一一加以很得体的批评。	The old ferryman rolled his small eyes and nodded, sizing up everything enviously and appreciatively, even offering fitting criticisms of every constituent part.
后来两人就坐到那还未完工的白木条凳上去，熟人又说到这碾坊的将来，似乎是团总女儿陪嫁的妆奁。	Then the two men took a seat on a still-unfinished bench.  The friend went on about this mill's future  it probably would be the dowry of the militia captain's daughter.
那人于是想起了翠翠，且记起大老托过他的事情来了，便问道：	Then he thought of Cuicui, and remembered something that Shunshun's No. 1 had asked him to do for him.  He inquired,
「伯伯，你翠翠今年十几岁？」	"Uncle, how old is Cuicui now?"
「满十四进十五岁。」老船夫说过这句话后，便接着在心中计算过去的年月。	"Thirteen, going on fourteen." Having said this, the old ferryman continued counting up the years and months to himself.
「十四岁多能干！将来谁得她真有福气！」	"What a clever girl for a thirteen-year-old! Whoever gets matched to her will be a lucky fellow!"
「有什么福气？又无碾坊陪嫁，一个光人。」	"How so? She doesn't have any such mill for a dowry. She'll go empty-handed."
「别说一个光人，一个有用的人，两只手抵得五座碾坊！洛阳桥也是鲁般两只手造的！－－」这样那样的说着，说到后来，那人笑了。	"Don't call her that, she's a hard worker. Her two hands are worth more than five mills! Lu Ban built the bridge at Luoyang with his two hands! " He went on, trying to refute the old ferryman, until he laughed at his own words.
老船夫也笑了，心想：「翠翠有两只手将来也去造洛阳桥吧，新鲜事！」	The old ferryman laughed too, thinking to himself: "Cuicui has two hands all right, but if she built a Luoyang Bridge, that would be a first!"
那人过了一会又说：	The other man paused and then said:
「茶峒人年青男子眼睛光，选媳妇也极在行。伯伯，你若不多我的心时，我就说个笑话给你听。」	"Young men here in Chadong have good eyes and they're very good at picking their wives. Uncle, if it wouldn't offend you, I'd like to tell you a funny little story."
老船夫问：「是什么笑话。」	"What funny story?" asked the old ferryman.
那人说：「伯伯你若不多心时，这笑话也可以当真话去听咧。」	The other said, "Uncle, don't be upset with me, but you can take this one seriously, if you want."
接着说的下去就是顺顺家大老如何在人家赞美翠翠，且如何托他来探听老船夫口气那么一件事。	He went on to say how No. 1 in Shunshun's family had praised Cuicui and sent him on an errand of inquiring about the old ferryman's opinion.
末了同老船夫来转述另一回会话的情形。	Finally he related another conversation he'd had.
「我问他：『大老，大老，你是说真话还是说笑话？』他就说：『你为我去探听探听那老的，我欢喜翠翠，想要翠翠，是真话！』	"I asked him, 'No. 1, are you in earnest or are you playing with me?' He replied, 'Go sound out the old man for me, will you?  I'm sweet on Cuicui, I long for her!  I mean it!'
我说：『我这口钝得很，说出了口老的一巴掌打来呢？』	So I said, 'I'm very blunt in expressing myself, and once I speak, I can't take it back  just suppose, what if the old man slaps me one?'
他说：『你怕打，你先当笑话去说，不会挨打的！』	He said, 'If you're afraid of his reaction, tell it first as something humorous.  That'll save you from any beating!'
所以，伯伯，我就把这件真事情当笑话来同你说了。	So you see, Uncle, this funny story I told you is about something real.
你试想想，他初九从川东回来见我时，我应当如何回答他？」	Think it over.  When he comes to see me after he returns from Eastern Sichuan on the ninth of the month, what should I tell him?"
老船夫记前一次大老亲口所说的话，知道大老的意思很真，且知道顺顺也欢喜欢翠翠，心里很高兴。	The old ferryman recalled what No. 1 had said in his own words during his last visit.  He knew that No. 1 had spoken frankly, and also that Shunshun liked Cuicui, so he was elated.
但这件事照规矩得这个人带封点心亲自到碧溪岨家中去说，方见得慎重起事，老船夫就说：「等他来时你说：老家伙听过了笑话后，自己也说了个笑话，他说，『车是车路，马是马路，各有走法。	But local custom said that No. 1 would have to come in person with gifts of cakes to Green Creek Hill and speak for himself to prove his seriousness.  The old ferryman said, "When he gets home, you tell him that after hearing your funny story, the old codger told one of his own  'In a game of chess, the chariot  the rook  moves one way and the horseman  the knight  another.
大老走的是车路，应当由大老爹爹作主，请了媒人来正正经经同我说。	If No. 1 wants to make his move directly like a chariot, his father ought to ask a go-between and put the proposition to me in the proper way.
走的是马路，应当自己作主，站在渡口对溪高崖上，为翠翠唱三年六个月的歌。』」	If he wants to move like a horseman, hurdling all obstacles, it's his play, to stand on the bluffs across the creek from the ferry and sing for Cuicui's heart until he's won her  for "three years and six months," if that's what it takes, as it says in the song.'"
「伯伯，若唱三年六个月的歌动得了翠翠的心，我赶明天就自己来唱歌了。」	"Uncle, if singing to her for three years and six months can move her heart, I'll start tomorrow and try to win her myself!"
「你以为翠翠肯了我还会不肯吗？」	"If Cuicui were willing, do you think I could refuse?"
「不咧，人家以为这件事你老人家肯了，翠翠便无有不肯呢。」	"That's not it. People think that if you make the decision, Cuicui can't object."
「不能那么说，这是她的事呵！」	"That's not right. This is about her!"
「便是她的事，可是必需老的作主，人家也仍然以为在日头月光下唱三年六个月的歌，还不如得伯伯说一句话好！」	"Even if it is, the elder has to have the final say. People will still think that singing three years and six months, be it under sunlight or moonlight, is less important than a good word from you!"
「那么，我说，我们就这样办，等他从川东回来时要他同顺顺去说明白。	"In that case, let's do it this way. When he returns home from Sichuan, have him talk it over with Shunshun.  Meanwhile, I'll ask Cuicui.
我呢，我也先问问翠翠；苦以为听了三年六个月的歌再跟那唱歌人走去有意思些，我就请你劝大老走他那弯弯曲曲的马路。」	If she prefers to follow a man who's sung for her three years and six months, I'll have to ask you to persuade No. 1 to choose that zigzag horseman's move."
「那好的。见了他我就说：『大老，笑话吗，我已说过了。真话呢，看你自己的命运去了。』	"Fine. When I see him, I'll say: 'No. 1, I told him the words in jest. As to the words in truth, that will depend on your fate.'
当真看他的命运去了，不过我明白他的命运，还是在你老人家手上捏着的。」	And so it will be, but I know that his fate still lies tightly within your grasp, old fellow."
「不是那么说！我若捏得定这件事，我马上就答应了。」	"That's not true! If it were within my grasp to decide this matter, I'd agree right away!"
这里两人把话说妥后，就过另一处看一只顺顺新近买来的三舱船去了。	With that settled, the two went to see a new, three-cabin boat that Shunshun had just purchased.
河街上顺顺吊脚楼方面，却有了如下事情。	Meanwhile, things had been going on in Shunshun's stilt house along River Street.
翠翠虽被那乡绅女孩喊到身边去坐，地位非常之好，从窗口望出去，河中一切朗然在望，然而心中可不安宁。	Cuicui had gone to sit near the daughter of the rich folk from the countryside.  Her location was spectacular; everything out on the river was clearly visible from the window, but Cuicui felt a little ill at ease.
挤在其他几个窗口看热闹的人，似乎皆常常把眼光从河中景物挪到这边几个人身上来。	The people who crowded around the other windows to see the excitement all seemed frequently to divert their gaze from the river to Cuicui and her company.
还有些人故意装成有别的事情样子，从楼这边走过那一边，事实上却全为得是好仔细看看翠翠这方面几个人。	Some even pretended to have some reason for passing by, when in fact they were just interested in sizing up these people Cuicui was sitting with.
翠翠心中老不自在，只想借故跑去。	Cuicui felt uneasy.  She just wanted an excuse to run away.
一会儿河下的炮声响了，几只从对河取齐的船只，直向这方面划来。	Soon a cannon sounded out on the river and several boats that had assembled on the farther shore rowed straight toward them.
先是四条船皆相去不远，如四枝箭在水面射着，到了一半，已有两只船占先了些，再过一会子，那两只船中间便又有一只超过了并进的船只而前。	Four boats took the lead in close formation, like four arrows shooting evenly through the water.
看看船到了税局门前时，第二次炮声又响，那船便胜利了。这时节胜利的已判明属于河街人所划的一只，各处便皆响着庆祝的小鞭炮。	Halfway across, two had already gone ahead of the others, and a little later, one of those pulled into the lead.  As the spectators saw it reach the customs house, another cannon shot announced the victory.  One could begin to make out that the winning boat was the one belonging to River Street.  Congratulatory firecrackers were heard all around.
那船于是沿了河街吊脚楼划去，鼓声蓬蓬作响，河边与吊脚楼各处，都同时呐喊表示快乐的祝贺。	The victors rowed past the stilt houses of River Street, their drum pounding as crowds along the streets and in the dangling foot houses shouted out joyous congratulations.
翠翠眼见在船头站定摇动小旗指挥进退头上包着红布的那个年青人，便是送酒葫芦到碧溪岨的二老，心中便印着三年前的旧事，「大鱼吃掉你！」	Cuicui noticed that the red-turbaned young man standing firmly in the prow, brandishing the little flag that gave the crew directions, was none other than No. 2  the one who had returned the gourd of wine to Green Creek Hill.  Her mind flashed back to events two years earlier. "A big fish might eat you!"
「吃掉不吃掉，不用你管！」「狗，狗，你也看人叫！」想起狗，翠翠才注意到自己身边那只黄狗，已不知跑到什么地方去，便离了座位，在楼上各处找寻她的黄狗，把船头人忘掉了。	"Whether it eats me or not, it's no concern of yours!" "All right, I won't worry about it!" "Hey, dog, save your barks for those who are worth it!" At that, Cuicui remembered the yellow dog that had come with her. She'd long since lost him, so she got up from her place and searched all over the house, completely forgetting the young man in the prow of the boat.
她一面在人丛里找寻黄狗，一面听人家正说些什么话。	As she looked for her dog in the crowd, she overheard some conversations.
一个大脸妇人问：「是谁家的人，坐到顺顺家当中窗口前的那块好地方？」	A woman with a broad face asked, "Whose family is she from, to get that prime seat in front of a window at Shunshun's house?"
一个妇人就说：「是砦子上王乡绅家大姑娘，今天说是来看船，其实来看人，同时也让人看！	Another woman responded, "She's the daughter of the country gentleman Wang up in one of the stockades. They say they came to see the boats, but really they're here to look over people  and be looked at!
人家命好，有福分坐那好地方！」	They must be something, to merit such a good place!"
「看谁人？被谁看？」	"Who's come to look at whom?"
「嗨，你还不明白，那乡绅想同顺顺打亲家呢。」	"Goodness, don't you know  that country gentleman wants his daughter to marry into Shunshun's family."
「那姑娘配什么人？是大老，还是二老？」	"Who might they want to betroth to her? No. 1 or No. 2?"
「说是二老呀，等等你们看这岳云，就会上楼来看他丈母娘的！」	"No. 2. Just wait, and we'll see this Yue Yun come up and pay respects to his future mother-in-law!"
另一个女人便插嘴说：「事弄妥了，好得很呢！人家有一座崭新碾坊陪嫁，比十个长年还好一些。」	Another woman cut in: "The match is made, and it's a good one! The girl brings as dowry a brand-new mill by the river, which can do the work of ten hired laborers."
有人问：「二老怎么样？可乐意？」	Someone asked, "What does No. 2 think about that?"
有人就轻轻的说：「二老已说过了，这不必看。第一件事我就不想作那个碾坊的主人！」	Yet another person whispered, "No. 2 said, 'I don't need to look at her. To start with, I don't want to be a miller!'"
「你听岳云二老亲口说吗？」	"Did you hear Yue Yun say that?"
「我听别人说的。还说二老欢喜一个撑渡船的。」	"That's what someone told me. They also said that No. 2 likes that girl at the ferry."
「他又不是傻小二，不要碾坊，要渡船吗？」	"He's no dummy; if he doesn't want to be a miller, would he really want to be a ferryman?"
「那谁知道。横顺人是『牛肉炒韭菜，各人心里爱』，只看各人心里爱什么就吃什么。渡船不会不如碾坊！」	"Who knows? Anyway, as the saying goes, 'People eat what they like, even beef with chives.' A ferryboat needn't be any worse than a grain mill!"
当时各人眼睛对着河里，口中说着这些闲话，却无一个人回头来注意到身后边的翠翠。	They were all looking at the river as they gossiped, so no one noticed that Cuicui was right behind them.
翠翠脸发火发烧走到另外一处去，又听有两个人提到这件事。	Cuicui went away, her face burning with embarrassment, only to hear another pair of women talking about these same things.
且说：「一切早安排好了，只须要二老一句话。」又说：「只看二老今天那么一股劲儿，就可以猜想得出这劲儿是岸上一个黄花姑娘给他的！」	"Everything is settled. They're just waiting for No. 2 to give the word." And, "Just from the spirit that No. 2 showed in today's race, you could almost guess that he got it from a young maiden watching him from onshore!"
谁是激动二老的黄花姑娘？听到这个，翠翠心中不免有点儿乱。	Who was this young maiden who so moved No. 2?
翠翠人矮了些，在人背后已望不见河中情形，只听到敲鼓声渐近渐激越，岸上呐喊声自远而近，便知道二老的船恰恰经过楼下。	Cuicui was too short to see over the people and take in the river scenes now.  It was only from the swelling of the drumbeats as they drew nearer and more frantic, and the rise in hubbub from the crowd onshore, that she realized that No. 2's boat had rowed up to the house.
楼上人也大喊着，杂夹叫着二老的名字，乡绅太太那方面，且有人放小百子鞭炮。	People upstairs in the house were cheering, too, and calling out No. 2's name; over by the rich lady from the countryside, they were setting off strings of hundred-pop firecrackers.
忽然又用另外一种惊讶声音喊着，且同时便见许多人出门向河下走去。	Suddenly there arose other shouts, of astonishment and dismay, as a crowd of people went out the door to go down to the river.
翠翠不知出了什么事，心中有点迷乱，正不知走回原来座位边去好，还是依然站在人背后好。	Not knowing what had gone wrong, Cuicui felt a little confused.  She didn't know whether to go back to her original seat or keep standing in back of the spectators.
只见那边正有人拿了个托盘，装了一大盘粽子同细点心，在请乡绅太太小姐用点心，不好意思再过那边去，便想也挤出大门外到河下去看看。	But just then a tray full of zongzi and fine cakes was set before the rich country lady and her little miss, so Cuicui felt uncomfortable going back there.  She decided to squeeze out the door and see what was going on by the river.
从河街一个盐店旁边甬道下河时，正在一排吊脚楼的梁柱间，迎面碰头一群人，拥着那个头包红布的二老来了。	A passageway next to a salt company led from River Street down to the water, under overhanging beams and rafters.  She emerged head-on into a crowd of people swarming around No. 2 in his red turban.
原来二老因失足落水，已从水中爬起来了。	He had slipped and fallen into the water, but made his way out on his own.
路太窄了一些，翠翠虽闪过一旁，与迎面来的人仍然得肘子触着肘子。	Cuicui dodged to get out of the way, but the path was so narrow that she still found herself elbow-to-elbow with the oncoming surge of people.
二老一见翠翠就说：	No. 2 spotted Cuicui and said,
「翠翠，你来了，爷爷也来了吗？」	"Cuicui, you came! Did your grandfather come, too?"
翠翠脸还发着烧不便作声，心想：「黄狗跑到什么地方去了呢？」	Her face flushed crimson, Cuicui was too embarrassed to speak. She thought to herself, "Where has my yellow dog run off to?"
二老又说：	No. 2 continued:
「怎不到我家楼上去看呢？我已要人替你弄了个好位子。」	"Why not go up to my house to watch the proceedings? I told them to save you a good seat."
翠翠心想：「碾坊陪嫁，希奇事情咧。」	Cuicui thought to herself: "A mill for a dowry  how fine is that?"
二老不能逼迫翠翠回去，到后便各自走开了。	No. 2 couldn't persuade Cuicui to go back, so they went their separate ways.
翠翠到河下时，小小心中充满了一种说不分明的东西。	When she got to the river, her young heart was filled with feelings she could not understand.
是烦恼吧，不是！	Was she annoyed?  No!
是忧愁吧，不是！	Worried?  Not that, either.
是快乐吧，不，有什么事情使这个女孩子快乐呢？	Happy, then?  No, what would she be happy about?
是生气了吧，－－是的，她当真彷佛觉得自己是在生一个人的气，又像是在生自己的气。	Angry, perhaps.  Yes, that was it, she seemed to be angry at someone, and also at herself.
河边人太多了，码头边浅水中，船桅船篷上，以至于吊脚楼的柱子上，也莫不有人。	It was so crowded there by the river.
翠翠自言自语说：「人那么多，有什么三脚猫好看？	In the shallow waters by the docks, in the rigging and on the awnings of the boats, even among the support columns of the stilt houses, people were everywhere.
」先还以为可以在什么船上发现她的祖父，但搜寻了一阵，各处却无祖父的影子。	Cuicui mumbled to herself: "Why all the commotion? Did somebody find a three-legged cat?" She had hoped to find her grandfather on one of the boats, but after checking them all, she found no sign of him.
她挤到水边去，一眼便看到了自己家中那条黄狗，同顺顺家一个长年，正在去岸数丈一只空船上看热闹。	She jostled her way down to the riverbank and spotted the yellow dog enjoying the excitement with one of Shunshun's laborers in an empty boat a few yards from shore.
翠翠锐声叫喊了两声，黄狗张着耳叶昂头四面一望，便猛的扑下水中，向翠翠方面泅来了。	Cuicui called him twice in a shrill voice.  The yellow dog pricked up his ears and head, looking all around, before bounding into the river and swimming to Cuicui.
到了身边时狗身上已全是水，把水抖着且跳跃不已，翠翠便说：「得了，装什么疯。你又不翻船，谁要你落水呢？」	Soaked by the time he got to her, he shook himself and jumped up and down without cease, until Cuicui shouted, "Enough! What is this craziness, dog? Your boat didn't turn over. Who asked you to jump into the water?"
翠翠同黄狗找祖父去，在河街上一个木行前恰好遇着了祖父。	Cuicui and the yellow dog looked for Grandpa everywhere. They ran into him in front of a lumber store on River Street.
老船夫说：「翠翠，我看了个好碾坊，碾盘是新的，水车是新的，屋上稻草也是新的！	The old ferryman said, "Cuicui, I've just seen a first-rate grain mill! The millstone is new and so is the waterwheel  even the roof thatching is fresh!
水坝管着一绺水，急溜溜的，抽水闸时水车转得如陀螺。」	The dam releases water in such a raging torrent that when the sluice gate is pulled up, it gets the waterwheel to spinning like a top."
翠翠带着点做作问：「是什么人的？」	"Whose mill is it?" Cuicui asked, a little affectedly.
「是什么人的？住在山上的王团总的。	"Whose mill? Why, Squire Wang's, who lives up in the mountains at Middle Stockade, the militia captain.
我听人说是那中寨人为女儿作嫁妆的东西，好不阔气，包工就是七百吊大钱，还不管风车，不管家什！」	I've heard tell that it will be his daughter's dowry. Now that's extravagance for you.  Building it cost them seven hundred strings of cash, not including the windmill or the furnishings!"
「谁讨那个人家的女儿？」	"Who's going to marry his daughter?"
祖父望着翠翠干笑着，「翠翠，大鱼咬你，大鱼咬你。」	Grandpa looked at Cuicui and forced a smile. "A big fish is going to bite you. He'll bite you."
翠翠因为对于这件事心中有了个数目，便仍然装着全不明白，只询问祖父，「爷爷，谁个人得到那个碾坊？」	Precisely because she knew a thing or two about this matter, Cuicui pretended not to understand. She pressed Grandpa: "Grandfather, who will get that mill?"
「岳云二老！」祖父说了又自言自语的说，「有人羡慕二老得到碾坊，也有人羡慕碾坊得到二老！」	"No. 2, Yue Yun!" Grandpa said, also muttering to himself. "Some people envy No. 2 for getting the mill; others envy the mill for getting No. 2!"
「谁羡慕呢，爷爷？」	"Who's envious, Grandfather?"
「我羡慕。」祖父说着便又笑了。	"I'm envious," Grandpa said, with a smile.
翠翠说：「爷爷，你喝醉了。」	Cuicui said, "Grandfather, you're drunk."
「可是二老还称赞你长得美呢。」	"But No. 2 says you're very pretty."
翠翠说：「爷爷，你醉疯了。」	Cuicui: "Grandfather, you're crazy."
祖父说：「爷爷不醉不疯－－去，我们到河边看他们放鸭子去。」	Grandpa said, "Your grandfather is not drunk and he's not crazy. Come on, let's go down to the river and see them release the ducks. Too bad I'm too old to dive in and catch one to bring home and cook in a pot with ginger."
他还想说，「二老捉得鸭子，一定又会送给我们的。」话不及说，二老来了，站在翠翠面前微笑着。翠翠也微笑着。	He wanted to add: "If No. 2 catches a duck, he'll give it to us." But before he could say it, up came No. 2. He stood before Cuicui and smiled. Cuicui smiled back.
于是三个人回到吊脚楼上去。	The three of them went back up to the house on stilts.
第十一章	CHAPTER ELEVEN
有人带了礼物到碧溪岨，掌水码头的顺顺，当真请了媒人为儿子向渡船的攀亲起来了。	A man arrived at Green Creek Hill bearing gifts.  Dockmaster Shunshun had indeed asked a matchmaker to go to the ferry to seek matrimonial relations for his first son.
老船夫慌慌张张把这个人渡过溪口，一同到家里去。	Flustered, the old ferryman brought him across the creek and into the house.
翠翠正在屋门前剥豌豆，来了客并不如何注意。	Cuicui, who was shelling peas outside by the door, at first paid the guest little attention.
但一听到客人进门说「贺喜贺喜」，心中有事，不敢再待在屋门边，就装作追赶菜园地的鸡，拿了竹响篙唰唰的摇着，一面口中轻轻喝着，向屋后白塔跑去了。	But when she heard the matchmaker say, "Congratulations, congratulations," at the door, she began to worry. Unwilling to squat by the front door any longer, she pretended to be shooing away the chickens in the vegetable garden.  Flailing a bamboo whistling pole in the air, she softly scolded them as she ran toward the white pagoda in back.
来人说了些闲话，言归正传转述到顺顺的意见时，老船夫不知如何回答，只是很惊惶的搓着两只茧结的大手，好像这不会真有其事，而且神气中只像在说：「那好，那好，」其实这老头子却不曾说过一句话。	The visitor made small talk. When they got around to the matter at hand, namely Shunshun's initiative, the old ferryman didn't know how to respond. He could only rub his big, calloused hands together, as if he couldn't believe it. The expression on his face seemed to say: "Fine, this is wonderful," yet the old man said not a word in reply.
马兵把话说完后，就问作祖父的意见怎么样。	When the visitor finished, he asked Grandpa what he thought about it.
老船夫笑着把头点着说：「大老想走车路，这个很好。可是我得问问翠翠，看她自己主意怎么样。」来人走后，祖父在船头叫翠翠下河边来说话。	The old ferryman smiled and nodded: "So No. 1 wants to make the chariot's move, that's just fine. But I must ask Cuicui, to get her reaction." After he had seen off the visitor, Grandpa stood in the prow of the boat and called Cuicui down to the river for a talk.
翠翠拿了一簸箕豌豆下到溪边，上了船，娇娇的问他的祖父：「爷爷，你有什么事？」祖父笑着不说什么，只偏着个白发盈颠的头看着翠翠，看了许久。	Bringing a pan of peas down with her to the stream, Cuicui boarded the boat and asked her grandpa, with all the charm she could muster, "Grandfather, what is it?" Grandpa smiled in silence. Tilting his hoary white head, he looked at Cuicui for a long time. Cuicui sat down in the boat, a little taken aback.
翠翠坐到船头，低下头去剥豌豆，耳中听着远处竹篁里的黄鸟叫。	She bent over to continue shelling her peas when she heard the call of a yellow finch from the bamboo grove.
翠翠想：「日子长咧，爷爷话也长了。」翠翠心轻轻的跳着。	Cuicui thought: "The days are growing longer, and Grandfather is taking longer to get his words out, too." Her heart was gently pounding.
过了一会祖父说：「翠翠，翠翠，先前来的那个伯伯来作什么，你知道不知道？」	After another pause, Grandpa said: "Cuicui  Cuicui  do you know what that visit was all about?"
翠翠说：「我不知道。」说后脸同颈脖全红了。	Cuicui answered, "No, I don't." But her face and neck flushed crimson.
祖父看看那种情景，明白翠翠的心事了，便把眼睛向远处望去，在空雾里望见了十五年前翠翠的母亲，老船夫心中异常柔和了。轻轻的自言自语说：「每一只船总要有个码头，每一只雀儿得有个巢。」	Observing all this, Grandpa sensed Cuicui's anxiety and looked up far away across the sky. In the mist he saw Cuicui's mother as she was fifteen years earlier, and his heart melted.  He said, under his breath, "Every boat needs a berth, and every sparrow needs a nest."
他同时想起那个可怜的母亲过去的事情，心中有了一点隐痛，却勉强笑着。	He began to think about the unhappy fate of Cuicui's mother. His heart ached and he smiled with difficulty.
翠翠呢，正从山中黄鸟杜鹃叫声里，以及山谷中伐竹人唦唦一下一下的砍伐竹子声音里，想到许多事情。	And Cuicui  Cuicui was thinking about so many things, amid the calls of the finches and cuckoo birds in the mountains and the chops of lumbermen felling bamboos in the valleys.
老虎咬人的故事，与人对骂时四句头的山歌，造纸作坊中的方坑，铁工厂熔铁炉里泄出的铁汁－－耳朵听来的，眼睛看到的，她似乎都要去温习温习。	Stories of tigers eating people, and the mountain songs people sang to belittle and make fun of each other, the square pit in which papermakers mixed their pulp, the molten iron that flowed out of a foundry smelting furnace  she felt compelled to recollect everything her ears had heard and her eyes had seen.
她其所以这样作，又似乎全只为了希望忘掉眼前的一桩事而起。	It seemed to be her way of putting aside the present matter and wishing it away.
但她实在有点误会了。	And yet she misunderstood what was really going on.
祖父说：「翠翠，船总顺顺家里请人来作媒，想讨你作媳妇，问我愿不愿。我呢，人老了，再过三年两载会过去的，我没有不愿的事情。这是你自己的事，你自己想想，自己来说。愿意，就成了；不愿意，也好。」	Grandpa said: "Cuicui, Fleetmaster Shunshun's family invited a matchmaker to ask for you as their daughter-in-law. They sought my permission. But I'm old.  I might pass from the scene a couple of years from now, so it's not fit for me to delay things. This is all about you.  You think it over and you give me your decision. If you're willing, then it's settled.  If not, that's all right, too."
翠翠不知如何处理这个问题，装作从容，怯怯的望着老祖父。	Cuicui had no idea what to do.  Pretending to be unruffled, she timidly eyed her old grandpa.
又不便问什么，当然也不好回答。	She didn't feel like asking for an explanation, and certainly not like giving an answer.
祖父又说：「大老是个有出息的人，为人又正直，又慷慨，你嫁了他，算是命好！」	Grandpa added: "No. 1 is a man of good prospects. He's fair-minded and generous. If you marry him, you can say you're blessed with good fate!"
翠翠明白了，人来做媒的大老！	Cuicui understood for the first time: the intended match was with No. 1!
不曾把头抬起，心忡忡的跳着，脸烧得厉害，仍然剥她的豌豆，且随手把空豆菜抛到水中去，望着它们在流水中从从容容的流去，自己也俨然从容了许多。	She didn't raise her head. Her heart beat fast and her face burned as she went on shelling her peas, from time to time throwing empty pods into the creek and watching them drift slowly downstream, as if she had calmed down.
见翠翠总不作声，祖父于是笑了，且说：	Grandpa responded to Cuicui's silence with a smile.
「翠翠，想几天不碍事。	"Cuicui, it's fine if you want to think it over for a few days.
洛阳桥并不是一个晚上造得好的，要日子咧。	Luoyang Bridge wasn't built overnight.
前次那人来的就向我说到这件事，我已经就告过他：车是车路，马是马路，各有规矩。	You've got time.  When No. 1 came the time before, he spoke to me about this and I told him then: chariots have to move like chariots, and horsemen like horsemen, according to the rules.
想爸爸作主，请媒人正正经经来说是车路；要自己作主，站到对溪高崖竹林里为你唱三年六个月的歌是马路，－－你若欢喜走马路，我相信人家会为你在日头下唱热情的歌，在月光下唱温柔的歌，一直唱到吐血喉咙烂！」	If his father was going to take charge of this, he had to have a matchmaker do it according to custom  that's how chariots move; if he wanted to take charge of it himself, he had to go up into the bamboo grove on the bluffs across the creek and sing for you, three years and six months  that's the horseman's move.  If you prefer the horseman's move, I'm sure he'll sing passionate songs during the day and tender ones in the moonlight, like a nightingale, singing his throat out until he spits blood!"
翠翠不作声，心中只想哭，可是也无理由可哭。	Cuicui remained silent.  She felt like crying, but for no apparent reason.
祖父再说下去，便引到死去了的母亲来了。	Grandpa got to talking again, and now he came to Cuicui's dead mother.
老人说了一阵，沉默了。	After a while, he fell silent.
翠翠悄悄把头撂过一些，祖父眼中业已酿了一汪眼泪。	Dipping her head in sadness, Cuicui could see tears in her grandpa's eyes.
翠翠又惊又怕怯生生的说：「爷爷，你怎么的？」祖父不作声，用大手掌擦着眼睛，小孩子似的咕咕笑着，跳上岸跑回家中去了。	Upset and afraid, she fearfully asked him, "Grandfather, what's the matter?" Without saying a word, Grandpa clumsily wiped his eyes with the palm of his hand. He jumped ashore and ran home, giggling like a little boy.
翠翠心中乱乱的，想赶去却不赶去。	Upset, Cuicui couldn't bring herself to run after him.
雨后放晴的天气，日头炙到人肩上背上已有了点儿力量。	As it cleared up after the rain, the sun beat down painfully on people's backs and shoulders.
溪边芦苇水杨柳，菜园中菜蔬，莫不繁荣滋茂，带着一分有野性的生气。	The reeds and water-willow shrubs by the creek, like the vegetables in the garden, ran riot, bearing a hint of wild vitality.
草丛里绿色蚱蜢各处飞着，翅膀搏动空气时窸窸作声。	Green grasshoppers flew among the thick grasses, their wings setting a stir in the wind.
枝头新蝉声音已渐渐洪大。	Newly emerged cicadas on the branches had not yet set up a din, but their noise was gradually strengthening.
两山深翠逼人竹篁中，有黄鸟与竹雀杜鹃鸣叫。	In the stunning verdure of the emerald bamboo groves on the mountains, yellow finches, bamboo finches, and cuckoos sang in turn.
翠翠感觉着，望着，听着，同时也思索着：	Cuicui looked and listened, took it all in, and also reflected:
「爷爷今年七十岁－－三年六个月的歌－－谁送那只白鸭子呢？－－得碾子的好运运气，碾子得谁更是好运运气？－－」	"Grandfather is seventy this year  three years and six months  who gave us that white duck?  what luck to get that mill, or is the mill even luckier to get him? "
痴着，忽地站运气，半簸箕豌豆便倾倒到水中去了。	In her own little world, she stood up abruptly, spilling half her pan of peas into the creek.
伸手把那簸箕从水中捞运气时，隔溪有人喊过渡。	As she retrieved the pan from the water, someone hailed the ferry from the other shore.
第十二章	CHAPTER TWELVE
翠翠第二天在白塔下菜园地里，第二次被祖父询问到自己主张时，仍然心儿忡忡的跳着，把头低下不作理会，只顾用手去掐葱。	The next day, Cuicui was in the vegetable garden below the white pagoda again when Grandpa asked for her decision.  Her heart still pounding, she bowed her head as if she hadn't heard and went on picking her scallions.
祖父笑着，心想：「还是等等看，再说下去这一坪葱会全掐掉了。」同时似乎又觉得这其间有点古怪处，不好再说下去，便自己按捺到言语，用一个做作的笑话，把问题引到另外一件事情上去了。	Grandpa smiled and thought: "I'd better wait till later. If I keep at her, she'll pick every scallion in sight!" Yet he also sensed something strange in her manner. He couldn't very well continue in this vein, so he stifled his words and changed the subject with a contrived joke.
天气渐渐的越来越热了。	The weather was warming day by day.
近六月时，天气热了些，老船夫把一个满是灰尘的黑陶缸子从屋角隅里搬出，自己还匀出闲工夫，拼了几方木板作成一个圆盖。	It was hot by the time the sixth month drew near. The old ferryman found time to drag a black earthenware vat covered with dust out of the corner of the house and piece together some wood slats to make a round lid for it.
又锯木头作成一个三脚架子，且削刮了个大竹筒，用葛藤系定，放在缸边作为舀茶的家具。	He also took out his saw and made a tripod stand, whittled a big bamboo tube as a ladle for dipping out tea, then tied it to the vat with kudzu vine.
自从这茶缸移到屋门溪边后，每早上翠翠就烧一大锅开水，倒进那缸子里去。	After he'd moved this vat out the door to the stream bank, Cuicui would boil a big pot of water every morning to make tea.
有时缸里加些茶叶，有时却只放下一些用火烧焦的锅巴，乘那东西还燃着时便抛进缸里去。	Sometimes she'd add tea leaves; other times, she'd just drop in some burned crusts from their cooked rice.
老船夫且照例准备了些发痧肚痛治泡疮疡子的草根木皮，把这些药搁在家中当眼处，一见过渡人神气不对，就忙匆匆的把药取来，善意的勒迫这过路人使用他的药方，且告人这许多救急丹方的来源（这些丹方自然全是他从城中军医同巫师学来的）。	The old ferryman, as was his custom, prepared native cures from roots and tree bark to heal sunstroke, stomachaches, blisters, and sores.  He kept these medicines close at hand.  The moment he saw a passenger who didn't look right, he'd press the traveler to try his remedies, relating the source of his many prescriptions (it went without saying that he learned them from the medics and spirit healers in town).
他终日裸着两只膀子，在方头船上站定，头上还常常是光光的，一头短短白发，在日光下如银子。	Bare-armed the day long, he stood firm in his square-nosed ferryboat, often bare-headed, too, his short, white hair shining like silver in the sunlight.
翠翠依然是个快乐人，屋前屋后跑着唱着，不走动时就坐在门前高崖树荫下吹小竹管儿玩。	Cuicui acted happy, running around outside the house singing.  When not on the move, she sat in front of the house on the high bluffs, in the shade, playing her little bamboo flute.
爷爷彷佛把大老提婚的事早已忘掉，翠翠自然也早忘掉这件事情了。	Grandfather acted as if he had completely forgotten No. 1's marriage proposal, so of course Cuicui did, too.
可是那做媒的不久又来探口气了，依然是同从前一样，祖父把事情成否全推到翠翠身上去，打发了媒人上路。	But before long the matchmaker returned to sound them out.
回头又同翠翠谈了一次，也依然不得结果。	As before, Grandpa relegated the matter to Cuicui and sent the go-between back.  Later he had another talk with Cuicui, again without any resolution.
老船夫猜不透这事情在这什么方面有个疙瘩，解除不去，夜里躺在床上便常常陷入一种沉思里去，隐隐约约体会到一件事情－－翠翠爱二老不爱大老，想到了这里时，他笑了，为了害怕而勉强笑了。	The old ferryman couldn't guess what the obstacle was, or how to fix it.  He'd lie in bed, mulling it over until finally it began to occur to him that perhaps Cuicui loved the younger brother, not the elder.  That made him smile, an unnatural smile from fear.
其实他有点忧愁，因为他忽然觉得翠翠一切全像那个母亲，而且隐隐约约便感觉到这母女二人共同的命运。	In truth he was a little worried, because it suddenly occurred to him that Cuicui was like her mother in every way.  He had a vague feeling that mother and daughter would share the same fate.
一堆过去的事情蜂拥而来，不能再睡下去了，一个人便跑出门外，到那临溪高崖上去，望天上的星辰，听河边纺织娘以及一切虫类如雨的声音，许久许久还不睡觉。	Events of the past swarmed into his mind and he could no longer sleep.  He ran out the door alone, onto the high bluffs by the creek.  He looked up at the stars and listened to the katydids and sounds of the other insects, constant as rain.  He could not sleep for a very long time.
这件事翠翠是毫不注意的，这小女孩子日里尽管玩着，工作着，也同时为一些很神秘的东西驰骋她那颗小小的心，但一到夜里，却甜甜的睡眠了。	Cuicui, of course, was unaware of this. A young girl whose days were always filled with play and work, she felt something very mysterious racing within her little heart, but when night came, she went peacefully to sleep.
不过一切皆得在一份时间中变化。	And yet, everything changes with time.
这一家安静平凡的生活，也因了一堆接连而来的日子，在人事上把那安静空气完全打破了。	This family's quiet and ordinary life, as days came and went in succession, saw the peace in its human affairs completely broken.
船总顺顺家中一方面，则天保大老的事已被二老知道了，傩送二老同时也让他哥哥知道了弟弟的心事。	In Fleetmaster Shunshun's household, Tianbao's actions were already known to No. 2, and Nuosong let his elder brother know what was on his mind, too.
这一对难兄难弟原来同时爱上了那个撑渡船的外孙女。	They were brothers in the hardships of love, both loving the granddaughter of a ferryman.
这事情在本地人说来并不希奇，边地俗话说：「火是各处可烧的，水是各处可流的，日月是各处可照的，爱情是各处可到的。」	This did not seem at all peculiar to the local folk.  A common saying in the borderlands was: "Fire can burn and water can flow anywhere; sunshine and moonshine also reach everywhere; and so, too, does love."
有钱船总儿子，爱上一个弄渡船的穷人家女儿，不能成为希罕的新闻，有一点困难处，只是这两兄弟到了谁应取得这个女人作媳妇时，是不是也还得照茶峒人规矩，来一次流血的挣扎？	It was not remarkable that the sons of a rich fleetmaster had fallen in love with the granddaughter of a poor ferryman. There was one problem.  Would the brothers decide who would marry the girl by the usual Chadong practice of a bloody struggle?
兄弟两人在这方面是不至于动刀的，但也不作兴有「情人奉让」如大都市懦怯男子爱与仇对面时作出的可笑行为。	These brothers would never take up arms against each other, but neither were they accustomed to "yielding in the contest of love," like the laughable behavior of cowardly city males when faced with matters of love and hate.
那哥哥同弟弟在河上游一个造船的地方，看他家中那一只新船，在新船旁把一切心事全告给了弟弟，且附带说明，这点爱还是两年前植下根基的。	The elder took his younger brother to a shipbuilder's yard upstream to see the family's new boat, then told the younger boy all that was in his heart, adding that his affection had been growing for two years.
弟弟微笑着，把话听下去。	The younger brother heard him out with a smile on his face.
两人从造船处沿了河岸又走到王乡绅新碾坊去，那大哥就说：	The two boys followed the riverbank from the shipyard to Squire Wang's new grain mill.  The elder brother said:
「二老，你倒好，作了团总女婿，有座碾坊；我呢，若把事情弄好了，我应当接那个老的手来划渡船了。	"No. 2, you're lucky to be Militia Captain Wang's prospective son-in-law and have this mill; as for me, if I do things right, I'll be inheriting from that old man the right to row a ferryboat.
我欢喜这个事情，我还想把碧溪岨两个山头买过来，在界在线种大南竹，围着这一条小溪作为我的砦子」	But I'd like that.  I'd like to buy up the two hills at Green Creek Hill and plant stands of bamboo around the boundaries, fencing us in at our own little fortress by the stream!"
那二老仍然的听着，把手中拿的一把弯月形镰刀随意斫削路旁的草木，到了碾坊时，却站住了向他哥哥说：	No. 2 continued listening in silence. He hacked at grasses and shrubs by the roadside with his sickle. When they reached the mill, he stopped and told his brother:
「大老，你信不信这女子心上早已有了个人？」	"Elder Brother, would you believe me if I told you that this girl already has her heart set on another, and has for some time?"
「我不信。」	"Not a chance."
「大老，你信不信这碾坊将来归我？」	"Elder Brother, do you think this mill was meant for me?"
「我不信。」	"No."
两人于是进了碾坊。	They entered the millhouse.
二老说：「你不必－－大老，我再问你，假若我不想得这座碾坊，却打量要那只渡船，而且这念头也是两年前的事，你信不信呢？」	No. 2 continued: "Now don't  Well, Elder Brother, let me ask you again, suppose I didn't want this mill, but that ferryboat instead, and suppose, too, that I'd got this idea two years ago  would you believe that?"
那大哥听来真着了一惊，望了一下坐在碾盘横轴上的傩送二老，知道二老不是开玩笑，于是站近了一点，伸手在二老肩上拍打了一下，且想把二老拉下来。	Startled, the elder brother stared at his younger brother, Nuosong, sitting there on the horizontal axle of the mill roller.  Realizing that No. 2 was telling him what was in his heart, he came up to him and clapped him on the shoulder, as if to bring him down to the ground.
他明白了这件事，他笑了。	He understood now, and laughed.
他说，「我相信的，你说的是真话」	He said: "Now I believe you. Everything you've said is true!"
二老把眼睛望着他的哥哥，很诚实的说：	No. 2 looked back at his brother and said, with utter frankness:
「大老，相信我，这是真事。我早就那么打算到了。家中不答应，那边若答应了，我当真预备去弄渡船的！	"Elder Brother, believe me, this is the truth. This has been my plan for some time now. If her family agrees, even if ours doesn't, I truly mean to be a ferryman!
－－你告我，你呢？」	What about you, then?"
「爸爸已听了我的话，为我要城里的杨马兵做保山，向划渡船说亲去了」大老说到这个求亲手续时，好像知道二老要笑他，又解释要保山去的用意，只是因为老的说车有车路，马有马路，我就走了车路。	"Papa has already acted on my behalf. He had Horseman Yang come from town to be my matchmaker and deliver my proposal to the ferryman!" When No. 1 got to the part about how he went about it, as if aware that No. 2 might laugh at him, he explained why he wanted a go-between to do it: "You see, the old man said that chariots must move like chariots and horsemen must move like horsemen. So I adopted the direct way, the chariot's move."
「结果呢？」	"What was the response?"
「得不到什么结果。老的口上含李子，说不明白。」	"There's none yet. The old man talked out of both sides of his mouth."
「马路呢？」	"What about adopting the horseman's move?"
「马路呢，那老的说若走马路，得在碧溪岨对溪高崖上唱三年六个月的歌。	"The old man said that the horseman's move means singing for the girl from the bluffs across the creek for three years and six months.
把翠翠心唱软，翠翠就归我了。」	If I could bend Cuicui's heart toward me, she'd be mine."
「这并不是个坏主张」	"What a good idea!"
「是呀，一个结巴人话说不出还唱得出。可是这件事轮不到我了。我不是竹雀，不会唱歌。	"Maybe. Sometimes a stutterer can sing what he can't say. But that's not me. I'm no song sparrow; I haven't got the voice.
鬼知道那老的存心是要把孙女儿嫁个会唱歌的水车，还是预备规规矩矩嫁个人」	Who the hell knows whether the old man would rather marry his granddaughter to a singing waterwheel or to a real man!"
「那你怎么样？」	"What are you going to do, then?"
「我想告那老的，要他说句实在话。只一句话。	"I'd like to see the old man and get a straight answer out of him. Just get the word. If 'No,' I'll take a boat downstream to Taoyuan.
不成，我跟船下桃源去了；成呢，便是要我撑渡船，我也答应了他。」	If 'Yes,' I'll agree, even if it means tugging that ferryboat."
「唱歌呢？」	"Would you sing for her?"
「这是你的拿手好戏，你要去做竹雀你就去吧，我不会捡马粪塞你嘴巴的。」	"Younger Brother, that's your strong suit. If you want to be a song sparrow, hurry up and get to it. I won't stuff your mouth with horse manure."
二老看到哥哥那种样子，便知道为这件事哥哥感到的是一种如何烦恼了。	No. 2 could tell how upset his elder brother was.
他明白他哥哥的性情，代表了茶峒人粗卤爽直一面，弄得好，掏出心子来给人也很慷慨作去，弄不好，亲舅舅也必一是一二是二。	He knew his temper, which embodied the rough, straightforward side of the Chadong folk.  In the right circumstances, he'd tear out his heart for you; cross him, and he'd battle his own maternal uncle blow for blow.
大老何尝不想在车路上失败时走马路；但他一听到二老的坦白陈述后，他就知道马路只二老有分，自己的事不能提了。	If No. 1 met with failure after making the chariot's move, surely he would want to try the horseman's.  But once he'd heard his younger brother's frank profession, he realized that No. 2 would best him at the latter approach.  No. 1 hadn't a chance.
因此他有点运气恼，有点愤慨，自然是无从掩饰的。	Hence he was a little offended, a little indignant, and he couldn't hide it.
二老想出了个主意，就是两兄弟月夜里同到碧溪岨去唱歌，莫让人知道是弟兄两个，两人轮流唱下去，谁得到回答，谁便继续用那张唱歌胜利的嘴唇，服侍那划渡船的外孙女。	No. 2 had an idea: let the brothers go together to sing at Green Creek Hill one moonlit night, without letting on that there were two of them.
大老不善于唱歌，轮到大老时也仍然由二老代替。	They would sing in turn and whoever got a song in response could let his victorious lips take up the refrain for the ferryman's granddaughter.  Since No. 1 was not much of a singer, when it was his turn, No. 2 would sing for him.
两人运气命运来决定自己的幸福，这么办可说是极公平了。	What could be fairer than to let fate decide their future happiness?
提议时，那大老还以为他自己不会唱，也不想请二老替他作竹雀。	When he heard this proposal, No. 1, thinking that he could not sing for himself, didn't want his younger brother to be the song sparrow in his place.
但二老那种诗人性格，却使他很固持的要哥哥实行这个办法。	But No. 2, being of a poetic disposition, stubbornly insisted on this solution.
二老说必需这样作，一切才公平一点。	He said this was the only way, for it was completely fair and impartial.
大老把弟弟提议想想，作了一个苦笑。	No. 1 thought about his younger brother's suggestion some more and smiled wryly.
「×娘的，自己不是竹雀，还请老弟做竹雀！好，就是这样子，我们各人轮流唱，我也不要你帮忙，一切我自己来吧。	"Damn it all! I'm no songbird  so I'm going to ask my little brother to be one for me? All right, let's do it this way: we'll take turns singing, but I don't want any help from you.  I'll do all my own singing.
树林子里的猫头鹰，声音不动听，要老运气时，也仍然是自己叫下去，不请人帮忙的」	An owl in the forest can only screech, but when he wants a wife, he sings for himself, he doesn't hire a stand-in!"
两人把事情说妥当后，算算日子，今天十四，明天十五，后天十六，接连而来的三个日子，正是有大月亮天气。	Once in agreement, they picked the date.  The moon would be fullest this night, the fourteenth, and the two nights following.
气候既到了中夏，半夜里不冷不热，穿了白家机布汗褂，到那些月光照及的高崖上去，遵照当地的习惯，很诚实与坦白去为一个「初生之犊」的黄花女唱歌。	It was midsummer; the nights were neither too hot nor too cool.  Wearing plain white homespun undershirts, they'd ascend the high bluffs where the moon shined bright and, according to local custom, truthfully and earnestly sing for the girl  an unspoiled maiden, made unafraid by her innocence.
露水降了，歌声涩了，到应当回家了时，就趁残月赶回家去。	When it was time for them to go home, as the dew fell and their voices grew weak, they would make their way back in the dimming moonlight.
