或过那些熟识的整夜工作不息的碾坊里去，躺到温暖的谷仓里小睡，等候天明。	Or they might stop at a familiar grain mill that operated all night without rest, lying down to sleep in the cozy barn until daybreak.
一切安排皆极其自然，结果是什么，两人虽不明白，但也看得极运气自然。	It was all so natural, and although neither brother could imagine the outcome, that would come just as naturally.
两人便决定了从当夜运气始，来作这种为当地习惯所认可的竞争。	They decided to do it that very night: engage in a competition honored by local custom.
第十三章	CHAPTER THIRTEEN
黄昏来时翠翠坐在家中屋后白塔下，看天空为夕阳烘成桃花色的薄云。	Cuicui sat beneath the white pagoda behind her house as dusk fell, watching wispy clouds in the sky burned peach-blossom pink by the setting sun.
十四中寨逢场，城中生意人过中寨收买山货的很多，过渡人也特别多，祖父在渡船上忙个不息。	The fourteenth of the month was market day at Middle Stockade. Many merchants from town went to that village fair to buy native products from the mountains, so ferry passengers were particularly abundant.  Grandpa worked on the ferryboat without rest.
天快夜了，别的雀子似乎都在休息了，只杜鹃叫个不息。	As nightfall descended, the songbirds fell quiet: only the cuckoos sang on without cease.
石头泥土为白日晒了一整天，草木为白日晒了一整天，到这时节皆放散一种热气。	The mud on the boulder had dried in the sun the day long, and so had the trees and grasses.  Now they were giving back their heat.
空气中有泥土气味，有草木气味，且有甲虫类气味。	The air smelled of damp soil, of the grasses and the trees, and also of beetles.
翠翠看着天上的红云，听着渡口飘乡生意人的杂乱声音，心中有些儿薄薄的凄凉。	Watching the pink clouds in the sky and listening to the jumble of voices from the merchants touring the countryside, Cuicui felt faintly despondent.
黄昏照样的温柔，美丽，平静。	The dusk was as serene as always, just as beautiful and peaceful.
但一个人若体念到这个当前一切时，也就照样的在这黄昏中会有点儿薄薄的凄凉。	Yet anyone in this situation would feel faintly despondent.
于是，这日子成为痛苦的东西了。	And so the days became a time of unhappiness.
翠翠觉得好像缺少了什么。	Cuicui felt that she was missing something.
好像眼见到这个日子过去了，想在一件新的人事上攀住它，但不成。	As she saw the days pass before her, she seemed to want to be caught up in a new kind of human relationship, yet it was beyond her.
好像生活太平凡了，忍受不住。	Life seemed too dull and ordinary.  She could bear it no longer.
「我要坐船下桃源县过洞庭湖，让爷爷满城打锣去叫我，点了灯笼火把去找我。」	"I want to sail a boat down past Taoyuan, across Lake Dongting. Let Granddad search for me all over town with a lantern, beating a gong and calling out my name."
她便同祖父故意生气似的，很放肆的去想到这样一件事，她且想象她出走后，祖父用各种方法寻觅全无结果，到后如何无可奈何躺在渡船上。	Letting her imagination run wild with this impossible development, she seemed purposely angry at Grandpa. She went on to imagine him searching for her everywhere to no avail, until finally he would lie down in his boat in defeat.
人家喊，「过渡，过渡，老伯伯，你怎么的，不管事！」「怎么的！翠翠走了，下桃源县了！」「那你怎么办？」「怎么办吗？拿把刀，放在包袱里，搭下水船去杀了她！」－－	Someone would shout, "Ferry me across, uncle. What's wrong with you? You're not doing your job!" "What's wrong? Cuicui is gone, she's gone down to Taoyuan County!" "What are you going to do about that?" "You know what? I'm going to pack a knife and catch a boat downstream, so I can kill her!"
翠翠彷佛当真听着这种对话，吓怕起来了，一面锐声喊着她的祖父，一面从坎上跑向溪边渡口去。	Cuicui became as frightened as if she had really heard such a conversation. She shrilly called out for her grandpa, running from the ridge to the creek where the ferry landing was.
见到了祖父正把船拉在溪中心，船上人喁喁说着话，小小心子还依然跳跃不已。	When she saw Grandpa in midstream, tugging his ferryboat while the passengers talked softly on board, her little heart leaped up and down.
「爷爷，爷爷，你把船拉回来呀！」	"Grandfather, pull the boat back to this side!"
那老船夫不明白她的意思，还以为是翠翠要为他代劳了，就说：	The old ferryman didn't understand what was on her mind. Thinking she wanted to take over for him, he said,
「翠翠，等一等，我就回来！」	"Cuicui, wait a little, I'll be back over!"
「你不拉回来了吗？」	"Why aren't you coming back now?"
「我就回来！」	"I'm coming right away!"
翠翠坐在溪边，望着溪面为暮色所笼罩的一切，且望到那只渡船上一群过渡人，其中有个吸旱烟的打着火镰吸烟，且把烟杆在船边剥剥的敲着烟灰，就忽然哭起来了。	Cuicui sat by the stream bank, observing everything out on the creek, which was now enveloped by the dusk. She also looked at the crowd of passengers on the ferryboat, including one who knocked the ashes out of his long-stemmed tobacco pipe by striking it against the side of the boat before lighting it with a sickle-shaped steel striker. She suddenly began to cry.
祖父把船拉回来时，见翠翠痴痴的坐在岸边，问她是什么事，翠翠不作声。	When Grandpa pulled the boat back to shore, he saw Cuicui sitting on the stream bank, staring into space.  He asked what was the matter, but Cuicui didn't reply.
祖父要她去烧火煮饭，想了一会儿，觉得自己哭得可笑，一个人便回到屋中去，坐在黑黝黝的灶边把火烧燃后，她又走到门外高崖上去，喊叫她的祖父，要他回家里来，在职务上毫不儿戏的老船夫，因为明白过渡人皆是赶回城中吃晚饭的人，来一个就渡一个，不便要人站在那岸边呆等，故不上岸来。	Grandpa wanted her to light the fire and prepare supper.  After thinking about it, Cuicui felt foolish for having wept.  She went alone back into the house. She sat down in the pitch-black kitchen and lit the fire, then went back outside onto the high bluffs and called out for her grandpa to come home. But he did not come ashore.  The old ferryman was too serious about his job for that.  He knew that his passengers were all hurrying back to town for their meals.  He ferried them as they came, one by one if necessary, so they wouldn't have to wait alone on the riverbank.
只站在船头告翠翠，且让他做点事，把人渡完事后，就回家里来吃饭。	Standing in the prow of the boat, he told Cuicui to stop yelling at him, to let him do his job.  When he had got his passengers across, he would return home and eat supper.
翠翠第二次请求祖父，祖父不理会，她坐在悬崖上，很觉得悲伤。	Cuicui again begged Grandpa to come, but he paid no attention. She sat on the bluffs, feeling quite put out.
天夜了，有一匹大萤火虫尾上闪着蓝光，很迅速的从翠翠身旁飞过去，翠翠想，「看你飞得多远！」便把眼睛随着那萤火虫的明光追去。	It was now completely dark. Blue light shone from the tail of a big firefly that flew past Cuicui in a burst of speed. She thought, "Let's see how far you can fly!" She followed the light with her eyes.
杜鹃又叫了。	Cuckoos began to sing again.
「爷爷，为什么不上来？我要你！」	"Grandfather, why don't you come back? I want you here!"
在船上的祖父听到这种带着娇有点儿埋怨的声音，一面粗声粗气的答道：「翠翠，我就来，我就来！」一面心中却自言自语：「翠翠，爷爷不在了，你将怎么样？」	When Grandpa heard her sweetly pleading voice, which bore a measure of reproach, he answered her gruffly: "I'm coming, Cuicui, I'm coming." Meanwhile he mumbled, under his breath, "Cuicui, when your grandfather is gone, what will you do then?"
老船夫回到家中时，见家中还黑黝黝的，只灶间有火光，见翠翠坐在灶边矮条凳上，用手蒙着眼睛。	When the old ferryman returned home, the kitchen was completely dark, lit only by flames from the stove. Cuicui was sitting there on a low stool, her face in her hands.
走过去才晓得翠翠已哭了许久。	When he came closer, he realized that Cuicui had been crying for quite a while.
祖父一个下半天来，皆弯着个腰在船上拉来拉去，歇歇时手也酸了，腰也酸了，照规矩，一到家里就会嗅到锅中所焖瓜菜的味道，且可见到翠翠安排晚饭在灯光下跑来跑去的影子。	Usually when Grandpa came home, stooped from pulling the boat all day long, with sore hands and an aching back, he'd smell vegetables stewing in the wok and see Cuicui dashing about in the lamplight, preparing supper.
今天情形竟不同了一点。	Today was a little different.
祖父说：「翠翠，我来慢了，你就哭，这还成吗？我死了呢？」	Grandpa continued, "Cuicui, I came in late, but is that any reason to cry? What if I were dead?"
翠翠不作声。	Cuicui said nothing.
祖父又说：「不许哭，做一个大人，不管有什么事都不许哭。要硬扎一点，结实一点，才配活到这块土地上！」	Grandpa went on: "No more crying! Act like an adult. No crying, no matter what. You have to be a little tougher, a little stronger, to get through life on this earth!"
翠翠把手从眼睛边移开，靠近了祖父身边去，「我不哭了。」	Cuicui uncovered her eyes and cuddled up to Grandpa. "I've stopped crying."
两人吃饭时，祖父为翠翠说到一些有趣味的故事。	While the two made supper, Grandpa told Cuicui some interesting stories.
因此提到了死去了的翠翠的母亲。	This led to talk of Cuicui's deceased mother.
两人在豆油灯下把饭吃过后，老船夫因为工作疲倦，喝了半碗白酒，因此饭后兴致极好，又同翠翠到门外高崖上月光下去说故事。	After they'd finished their meal by the light of a soybean-oil lamp, the old ferryman, tired from his day of work, drank half a bowl of liquor.  This picked up his spirits.  He went outside with Cuicui and told her some more stories under the moonlight out on the bluffs.
说了些那个可怜母亲的乖巧处，同时且说到那可怜母亲性格强硬处，使翠翠听来神往倾心。	He told her about how lovely and good her poor mother had been, and also about her stubborn streak.  Cuicui found it wholly absorbing.
翠翠抱膝坐在月光下，傍着祖父身边，问了许多关于那个可怜母亲的故事。	Listening in the moonlight next to her grandpa, with her arms wrapped around her knees, Cuicui asked for more stories about her poor mother.
间或吁一口气，似乎心中压上了些份量沉重的东西，想挪移得远一点，才吁着这种气，可是却无从把那东西挪开。	Sometimes she would sigh, as if something heavy were weighing on her heart that she could move away with her breath.  And yet she had no way to relieve her anxiety.
月光如银子，无处不可照及，山上篁竹在月光下皆成为黑色。	The moonlight was silvery and it shone everywhere.  The bamboo stands in the mountains appeared black under the moon.
身边草丛中虫声繁密如落雨。	From the thickets of grass came the chirping of insects, thick as rain.
间或不知道从什么地方，忽然会有一只草莺「落落落落嘘！」啭着它的喉咙，不久之间，这小鸟儿又好像明白这是半夜，不应当那么吵闹，便仍然闭着那小小眼儿安睡了。	Occasionally, a warbler suddenly twittered from some hidden place, until the little bird seemed to realize that it was too late to be making noise and closed its eyes to go peacefully to sleep.
祖父夜来兴致很好，为翠翠把故事说下去，就提到了本城人二十年前唱歌的风气，如何驰名于川黔边地。	Feeling in good spirits this night, Grandpa kept telling Cuicui his stories.  He told of how the local people's songs, twenty years ago, were famous throughout the borderlands of Sichuan and Guizhou.
翠翠的父亲，便是唱歌的第一手，能用各种比喻解释爱与憎的结子，这些事也说到了。	Cuicui's father was the best singer of them all, able to summon up every kind of figure of speech to explain the travails of love and hate  he told her all about that, too.
翠翠母亲如何爱唱歌，且如何同父亲在未认识以前在白日里对歌，一个在半山上竹篁里砍竹子，一个在溪面渡船上拉船，这些事也说到了。	He also told her how her mother had loved to sing, how she and Cuicui's father had sung love songs to each other in broad daylight before they ever met, one while cutting bamboo on the mountain, the other while tugging the ferryboat across the stream.
翠翠问：「后来怎么样？」	Cuicui asked: "Then what happened?"
祖父说：「后来的事长得很，最重要的事情，就是这种歌唱出了你。」	Grandpa answered: "That would take a long time to tell. The important thing is that these songs gave us you." After that, Grandpa fell silent. He did not add, "The songs gave us you, and then they took away your father and mother."
第十四章	CHAPTER FOURTEEN
老船夫做事累了睡了，翠翠哭倦了也睡了。	Exhausted by his work, the old ferryman slept.  Cuicui, tired from crying, slept too.
翠翠不能忘记祖父所说的事情，梦中灵魂为一种美妙歌声浮起来了，彷佛轻轻的各处飘着，上了白塔，下了菜园，到了船上，又复飞窜过悬崖半腰－－去作什么呢？	She could not forget the things Grandpa had spoken of. In her dreams, her soul drifted up on the strains of beautiful songs, seeming gently to float all about, up to the white pagoda, down to the vegetable garden, onto the boat  then it flew back, midway up the hanging bluffs  but for what purpose?
摘虎耳草！白日里拉船时，她仰头望着崖上那些肥大虎耳草已极熟习。	To pick the "tigers' ears": saxifrage! While pulling the boat during the daylight hours, she looked up at those cliffs and became quite familiar with the huge saxifrage leaves there.
崖壁三五丈高，平时攀折不到手，这时节却可以选顶大的叶子作桑	The cliffs were thirty or fifty feet high, ordinarily too high to reach, but now she could pick the very biggest leaf and make an umbrella out of it.
一切皆像是祖父说的故事，翠翠只迷迷胡胡的躺在粗麻布帐子里草荐上，以为这梦做得顶美顶甜。	Everything was happening just as in Grandpa's stories.  Cuicui drifted off as she lay on a reed mat inside the burlap mosquito netting, taking pleasure in the beauty and sweetness of her dream.
祖父却在床上醒着，张起个耳朵听对溪高崖上的人唱了半夜的歌。	Grandpa, however, lay awake on his bed, straining his ears listening to late-night singing on the high cliffs across the stream.
他知道那是谁唱的，他知道是河街上天保大老走马路的第一着，又忧愁又快乐的听下去。	He knew who was singing: it was No. 1, Tianbao of River Street, making the horseman's move.  He listened, both troubled and excited.
翠翠因为日里哭倦了，睡得正好，他就不去惊动她。	Having worn herself out from crying during the day, Cuicui slept soundly, so Grandpa didn't disturb her.
第二天天一亮，翠翠就同祖父起身了，用溪水洗了脸，把早上说梦的忌讳去掉了，翠翠赶忙同祖父去说昨晚上所梦的事情。	Cuicui and Grandpa rose at dawn the next day and washed their faces in the creek to remove the taboo against telling one's dreams the morning after. Then Cuicui hastened to tell Grandpa what she had dreamed the night before.
「爷爷，你说唱歌，我昨天就在梦里听到一种顶好听的歌声，又软又缠绵，我像跟了这声音各处飞，飞到对溪悬崖半腰，摘了一大把虎耳草，得到了虎耳草，我可不知道把这个东西交给谁去了。	"Grandfather, you told me stories about singing, and yesterday I heard the most beautiful songs in my dreams, soft and sweet.  I felt I was able to fly in the air with these songs, to the face of the cliffs across the creek, where I picked a big saxifrage leaf.  But once I picked it, I don't know who I gave it to.
我睡得真好，梦的真有趣」	I slept wonderfully and dreamed magnificently!"
祖父温和悲悯的笑着，并不告给翠翠昨晚上的事实。	Grandpa smiled gently in sympathy, but did not tell Cuicui what had gone on the night before.
祖父心里想：「做梦一辈子更好，还有人在梦里作宰相中状元咧。」	He thought to himself: "If only you could dream on forever. Some people become the prime minister in their dreams."
昨晚上唱歌的，老船夫还以为是天保大老，日来便要翠翠守船，借故到城里去送药，探听情况。	The old ferryman still thought it was Tianbao, No. 1, who had sung the night before.  In recent days he had asked Cuicui to take charge of the ferry.  Pretending to be delivering some medicines in town, he set off to find out what River Street was up to.  There he ran into No. 1.
在河街见到了大老，就一把拉住那小伙子，很快乐的说：	He drew the young man aside, saying, cheerfully,
「大老，你这个人，又走车路又走马路，是怎样一个狡猾东西」	"No. 1, you dog, now you've tried both the chariot's move and the horseman's move. You're a sly one!"
但老船夫却作错了一件事情，把昨晚唱歌人「张冠李戴」了。	But the old ferryman was wrong  he had confused one brother with the other.
这两弟兄昨晚上同时到碧溪岨去，为了作哥哥的走车路占了先，无论如何也不肯先开腔唱歌，一定得让那弟弟先唱。	The night before, the two brothers had come to Green Creek Hill together. Because the elder brother had already made the first move, in the role of chariot, he insisted on letting his younger brother sing first this time.
弟弟一开口，哥哥却因为明知不是敌手，更不能开口了。	Realizing from the moment the latter raised his voice in song that he could never match him, No. 1 was more reluctant than ever to sing himself.
翠翠同她祖父晚上听到的歌声，便全是那个傩送二老所唱的。	The songs that Cuicui and her grandpa heard that night were all sung by No. 2, Nuosong.
大老伴弟弟回家时，就决定了同茶峒地方离开，驾家中那只新油船下驶，好忘却了上面的一切。	As No. 1 accompanied his younger brother home, he decided to leave Chadong and go downstream on the family's new oil boat, the better to forget what had happened.
这时正想下河去看新船装货。	Just now, No. 1 was thinking of going to the docks to see cargo loaded onto the new boat.
老船夫见他神情冷冷的，不明白他的意思，就用眉眼做了一个可笑的记号，表示他明白大老的冷淡是装成的，表示他有消息可以奉告。	Noting his cold expression, the old ferryman, misunderstanding, gave an amused wink to let on that he knew that No. 1's cold-shouldering was pretend, and also to show that he had good news to impart.
他拍了大老一下，轻轻的说：	He clapped No. 1 on the back and whispered, sticking his thumb up,
「你唱得很好，别人在梦里听着你那个歌，为那个歌带得很远，走了不少的路！	"You sang so well that someone heard your songs in her dreams. The songs carried her far, far away, on many journeys!
你是第一号，是我们地方唱歌第一号。」	You're the best, the very best singer around!"
大老望着弄渡船的老船夫涎皮的老脸，轻轻的说：	No. 1 stared back at the old boatman's unabashed expression and whispered:
「算了吧，你把宝贝女儿送给了会唱歌的竹雀吧。」	"Enough. You can keep your precious granddaughter for some songbird."
这句话使老船夫完全弄不明白它的意思。	The old ferryman had no idea what he meant by that.
大老从一个吊脚楼甬道走下河去了，老船夫也跟着下去。	No. 1 went down a path between the stilt houses to the river, with the ferryman following.
到了河边，见那只新船正在装货，许多油篓子搁到岸边。	At the river, numerous bamboo oil casks were on the bank, waiting to be laded onto the new boat.
一个水手正在用茅草扎成长束，备作船舷上挡浪用的茅把，还有人在河边用脂油擦桨板。	A boatman was twisting strands of cogongrass into sheaves to make bulwarks that would keep waves from washing over the deck.  Another man was sitting on a rock by the riverbank, greasing the oars with his hands.
老船夫问那个坐在大太阳下扎茅把的水手，这船什么日子下行，谁押船。	The old ferryman asked the boatman making the grass bundles when the boat would launch and who would pilot it.  The boatman pointed to No. 1.
那水手把手指着大老。老船夫搓着手说：	The old ferryman rubbed his hands and said:
「大老，听我说句正经话，你那件事走车路，不对；走马路，你有分的」	"No. 1, let me speak seriously, the chariot's move is not the right one for you. But you'll succeed with the horseman's move!"
那大老把手指着窗口说：「伯伯，你看那边，你要竹雀做孙女婿，竹雀在那里啊」	No. 1 pointed his finger at a window above and said: "Uncle, look up there. If you want a songbird for your grand-son-in-law, there he is!"
老船夫抬头望到二老，正在窗口整理一个鱼网。	The old ferryman looked up and saw No. 2, who was mending a fishnet by the window.
回碧溪岨到渡船上时，翠翠问：	When the ferryman reached the ferry at Green Creek Hill, Cuicui asked him:
「爷爷，你同谁吵了架，脸色那样难看」	"Grandfather, you've been quarrelling with someone. You look awful!"
祖父莞尔而笑，他到城里的事情，不告给翠翠一个字。	Grandpa smiled, but said nothing about his trip to town.
第十五章	CHAPTER FIFTEEN
大老坐了那只新油船向下河走去了，留下傩送二老在家。	No. 1 took the new oil boat downriver, leaving Nuosong behind at home.
老船夫方面还以为上次歌声既归二老唱的，在此后几个日子里，自然还会听到那种歌声。	The old ferryman thought that since No. 2 had sung the time before, he would sing again in the days to come.
一到了晚间就故意从别样事情上，促翠翠注意夜晚的歌声。	After nightfall he made a point of getting Cuicui to listen for songs in the night air.
两人吃完饭坐在屋里，因屋前滨水，长脚蚊子一到黄昏就嗡嗡的叫着，翠翠便把蒿艾束成的烟包点燃，向屋中角隅各处晃着驱逐蚊子。	The two of them sat indoors after supper.  Because their home fronted on the water, long-legged mosquitoes began buzzing at dusk.  Cuicui lit bundles of wormwood incense and shook them in every corner of the house to drive away the insects.
晃了一阵，估计全屋子里已为蒿艾烟气熏透了，才搁到床前地上去，再坐在小板凳上来听祖父说话。	After shaking them until she thought the whole house was thoroughly smoked, she put some on the floor in front of her bed before sitting on a little wooden stool to listen to Grandpa tell his stories.
从一些故事上慢慢的谈到了唱歌，祖父话说得很妙。	The subject finally turned to singing, about which Grandpa was quite eloquent.
祖父到后发问道：	Finally, he asked Cuicui, jokingly:
「翠翠，梦里的歌可以使你爬上高崖去摘那虎耳草，若当真有谁来在对溪高崖上为你唱歌，你怎么样？」祖父把话当笑话说着的。	"Cuicui, the songs in your dream lifted you up the cliffs to pick saxifrage; if someone really sang to you from the cliffs across the stream, what would you do?"
翠翠便也当笑话答道：「有人唱歌我就听下去，他唱多久我也听多久！」	Cuicui answered him in a similarly humorous vein: "I'd listen to him, for as long as he could sing!"
「唱三年六个月呢？」	"What if he sang for three years and six months?"
「唱得好听，我听三年六个月。」	"If his voice was good, I'd listen for three years and six months."
「这不公平吧。」	"That's not fair."
「怎么不公平？为我唱歌的人，不是极愿意我长远听他的歌吗？」	"Why not? Wouldn't he want me to listen to him for a long time?"
「照理说：炒菜要人吃，唱歌要人听。	"They say that when you cook food, you want someone to eat it, and when you sing, you want someone to listen.
可是人家为你唱，是要你懂他歌里的意思！」	But if a person sings to you, it's because he wants you to understand the meaning of the lyrics!"
「爷爷，懂歌里什么意思？」	"Grandfather, what meaning?"
「自然是他那颗想同你要好的真心！不懂那点心事，不是同听竹雀唱歌一样了吗？」	"His true heart, of course, which wants your affection! If you don't grasp what's in his heart, would it be any better than listening to a songbird?"
「我懂了他的心又怎么样？」	"And what if I did happen to understand what's in his heart?"
祖父用拳头把自己腿重重的捶着，且笑着：「翠翠，你人乖，爷爷笨得很，话也不说得温柔，莫生气。	Grandpa slapped his thigh and laughed: "Cuicui, you're a smart girl and your grandfather is plain stupid. If I speak a little too bluntly, don't get mad at me.
我信口开河，说个笑话给你听。	I'll throw caution to the wind and tell you a funny story.
你应当当笑话听。河街天保大老走车路，请保山来提亲，我告给过你这件事了，你那神气不愿意，是不是？	No. 1, Tianbao of River Street, made the chariot's move; he had a go-between propose matrimony.  When I told you about it, you didn't seem too willing, am I right?
可是，假若那个人还有个兄弟，走马路，为你来唱歌，向你求婚，你将怎么说？」	But if he had a younger brother who adopted the horseman's move and sang to you to win your heart, what would you say to that?"
翠翠吃了一惊，低下头去。	Startled, Cuicui lowered her head.
因为她不明白这笑话有几分真，又不清楚这笑话是谁诌的。	She didn't know how much of this story might be real, or who made it up.
祖父说：「你告诉我，愿意哪一个？」	Grandpa said: "See if you can come up with an answer  which one do you prefer?"
翠翠便微笑着轻轻的带点儿恳求的神气说：	Forcing herself to smile, Cuicui replied softly, and somewhat pleadingly:
「爷爷莫说这个笑话吧。」翠翠站起身了。	"Grandfather, no more of your humor." She stood up.
「我说的若是真话呢？」	"Suppose it were not just a story but the truth?"
「爷爷你真是个－－」翠翠说着走出去了。	"Grandfather!" Cuicui walked away as she answered.
祖父说：「我说的是笑话，你生我的气吗？」	Grandpa said: "It was in jest! Are you angry at me?"
翠翠不敢生祖父的气，走近门限边时，就把话引到另外一件事情上去：「爷爷看天上的月亮，那么大！」说着，出了屋外，便在那一派清光的露天中站定。站了一忽儿，祖父也从屋中出到外边来了。	Cuicui could hardly be angry at him.  When she got to the door, she turned the conversation toward something else: "Look how big the moon is, Grandfather!" She went outside and stood still in the bright and open air. After a time, Grandpa came outside to join her.
翠翠于是坐到那白日里为强烈阳光晒热的岩石上去，石头正散发日间所储的余热。	Cuicui sat down on the great boulder  warmed by the hot sun during the day, it was radiating its spare heat now.
祖父就说：「翠翠，莫坐热石头，免得生坐板疮。」但自己用手摸摸后，自己便也坐到那岩石上了。	Grandpa said, "Cuicui, don't sit on the hot boulder or you'll get blisters." But after feeling the rock, he sat down on the crag, too.
月光极其柔和，溪面浮着一层薄薄白雾，这时节对溪若有人唱歌，隔溪应和，实在太美丽了。	The moonlight was very gentle and a thin white mist floated on top of the stream.  It would have been the perfect time for someone to sing from across the creek, and to be answered from the other side.
翠翠还记着先前祖父说的笑话。	Cuicui thought about the funny story her grandpa had told her.
耳朵又不聋，祖父的话说得极分明，一个兄弟走马路，唱歌来打发这样的晚上，算是怎么回事？	She was not deaf, and Grandpa had made his meaning quite clear.  What did it mean if one of the brothers made the horseman's move and spent a night like this singing to her?
她似乎为了等着这样的歌声，沉默了许久。	She remained silent for a long time, as if waiting to hear such songs.
她在月光下坐了一阵，心里却当真愿意听一个人来唱歌。	She sat there under the moonlight; she really wanted to be sung to.
久之，对溪除了一片草虫的清音复奏以外别无所有。	In the end, no sound came from the opposite bank other than the light drone of field insects.
翠翠走回家里去，在房门边摸着了那个芦管，拿出来在月光下自己吹着。	Cuicui went into the house and groped in the darkness for the luguan reed pipe.  She brought it back out into the moonlight and began blowing on it.
觉吹得不好，又递给祖父要祖父吹。	Feeling that her playing was not very good, she passed it to Grandpa.
老船夫把那个芦管竖在嘴边，吹了个长长的曲子，翠翠的心被吹柔软了。	The old ferryman put it to his lips and played a long tune that softened Cuicui's heart.
翠翠依傍祖父坐着，问祖父：	She sat beside her grandpa and asked:
「爷爷，谁是第一个做这个小管子的人？」	"Grandfather, who invented this little musical instrument?"
「一定是个最快乐的人，因为他分给人的也是许多快乐；可又像是个最不快乐的人作的，因为他同时也可以引起人不快乐！」	"It must have been the happiest person on earth, because happiness is what it gives; yet perhaps the world's unhappiest person, too, because it also makes people unhappy!"
「爷爷，你不快乐了吗？生我的气了吗？」	"Grandfather, are you unhappy? Are you angry at me?"
「我不生你的气。你在我身边，我很快乐。」	"Not at all. Having you by my side makes me very happy."
「我万一跑了呢？」	"What if I ran away?"
「你不会离开爷爷的。」	"You wouldn't leave your grandfather."
「万一有这种事，爷爷你怎么样？」	"But just suppose I did. What would you do?"
「万一有这种事，我就驾了这只渡船去找你。」	"In the remote event that you did, I'd go looking for you in this ferryboat."
翠翠嗤的笑了。	That brought a chortle from Cuicui.
「凤滩、茨滩不为凶，下面还有绕鸡笼；绕鸡笼也容易下，青浪滩浪如屋大。	Phoenix Rapids, Puncture Vine Rapids, aren't the worst to rage, Just go downstream and there is still the Twirling Chicken Cage; But Twirling Chicken Cage yet lacks the most ferocious foam, The waves at Green Foam Rapids are big as any home.
爷爷，你渡船也能下凤滩、茨滩、青浪滩吗？那些地方的水，你不说过像疯子吗？」	"Grandfather, could your ferryboat make it through all those rapids on the River Yuan? Didn't you say that the river in those places is like a madman, simply unwilling to listen to reason?"
祖父说：「翠翠，我到那时可真像疯子，还怕大水大浪？」	Grandpa said, "Cuicui, by the time I got there I'd be a madman myself. What would I have to fear from broad rivers and giant waves?"
翠翠俨然极认真的想了一下，就说：「爷爷，我一定不走。可是，你会不会走？你会不会被一个人抓到别处去？」	Cuicui thought it over a little, seemingly in earnest, then said: "Grandfather, I wouldn't leave. But would you? Might someone carry you off?"
祖父不作声了，他想到被死亡抓走那一类事情。	Grandpa didn't answer. He felt that he had nothing to fear from the law and the officials. Death was the one thing that might take him.
老船夫打量着自己被死亡抓走以后的情形，痴痴的看望天南角上一颗星子，心想：「七月八月天上方有流星，人也会在七月八月死去吧？」	The old ferryman got to thinking about what would happen when death carried him away.  Staring blankly at a star in the southern sky, he thought: "Shooting stars come only in the seventh and eighth months of the year. Might my death come then, too?"
又想起白日在河街上同大老谈话的经过，想其中寨人陪嫁的那座碾坊，想起二老，想起一大堆事情，心中有点儿乱。	He also thought about his conversation with No. 1 on River Street that day, about the mill that was to be the dowry of the girl from Middle Stockade, and about No. 2  about a lot of things. He felt a little uneasy at heart.
翠翠忽然说：「爷爷，你唱个歌给我听听，好不好？」	Suddenly, Cuicui asked: "Grandfather, won't you sing a song for me, please?"
祖父唱了十个歌，翠翠傍在祖父身边，闭着眼睛听下去，等到祖父不作声时，翠翠自言自语说：「我又摘了一把虎耳草了。」	Grandpa sang ten songs.  Cuicui listened by his side, her eyes closed. When he finished, she said to herself: "I've picked saxifrage again."
祖父所唱的歌便是那晚上听来的歌。	The songs Grandpa sang for her were the very songs they heard the night of her dream.
第十六章	CHAPTER SIXTEEN
二老有机会唱歌却从此不再到碧溪岨唱歌。	No. 2 now had his chance to serenade, but he never came to Green Creek Hill to sing again.
十五过去了，十六也过去了，到了十七，老船夫忍不住了，进城往河街去找寻那个年青小伙子，到城门边正预备入河街时，就遇着上次为大老作保山的杨马兵，正牵了一匹骡马预备出城，一见老船夫，就拉住了他：	The fifteenth passed, the sixteenth, then the seventeenth.  Unable to bear the wait any longer, the old ferryman went to town and looked for the young fellow on River Street.  When he got to the gate in the city wall and was about to enter River Street, he met Horseman Yang, who had been No. 1's matchmaker.  He was heading out of town, leading a mule, when he saw the old ferryman and took him aside:
「伯伯，我正有事情告你，碰巧你就来城里」	"Uncle, here you are come to town, just when I had something to discuss with you!"
「什么事？」	"What?"
「天保大老坐下水船到茨滩出了事，闪不知这个人掉到滩下漩水里就淹坏了。早上顺顺家里得到这个信，听说二老一早就赶去了。」	"That boat Tianbao took downstream was wrecked in the Puncture Vine Rapids. He fell into a whirlpool and drowned. Shunshun's family got the news this morning. I hear that No. 2 set off for the place at once."
这消息同有力巴掌一样重重的掴了他那么一下，他不相信这是当真的消息。	This bad news stung the old ferryman like a heavy slap in the face.  He couldn't believe it.
他故作从容的说：	Feigning calm, he said,
「天保大老淹坏了吗？从不听说有水鸭子被水淹坏的」	"No. 1, drowned? Since when does a duck drown in water?"
「可是那只水鸭子仍然有那么一次被淹坏了－－我赞成你的卓见，不让那小子走车路十分顺手。」	"But that's just what happened to this duck  I salute your wisdom in not letting that young fellow have your granddaughter so easily, by the chariot's move."
从马兵言语上，老船夫还十分怀疑这个新闻，但从马兵神气上注意，老船夫却看清楚这是个真的消息了。	The horse-soldier's words were not enough to still the old ferryman's doubts about the news, but he could clearly see from his expression that this was completely real.
他惨惨的说：	He said, grimly,
「我有什么卓见可言？这是天意！一切都有天意－－」老船夫说时心中充满了感情。	"What wisdom? This is the doing of Heaven! Everything is according to Heaven's will  " As he spoke, the old ferryman choked up.
特为证明那马兵所说的话有多少可靠处，老船夫同马兵分手后，于是匆匆赶到河街上去。	To confirm the reliability of the horse-soldier's news, the old ferryman took leave of him and hurried over to River Street.
到了顺顺家门前，正有人烧纸钱，许多人围在一处说话。	People were burning paper spirit money in front of Shunshun's house.  A crowd had gathered.
走近去听听，所说的便是杨马兵提到的那件事。	Pressing in among them, the ferryman heard them talking about the tragedy of which Horseman Yang had spoken.
但一到有人发现了身后的老船夫时，大家便把话语转了方向，故意来谈下河油价涨落情形了。	Yet, as soon as they discovered that the old ferryman was listening in, they all changed the subject, unnaturally, to the price of oil in downstream markets.
老船夫心中很不安，正想找一个比较要好的水手谈谈。	Nervous and worried, the old ferryman looked around for a boatman with whom he could talk on friendlier terms.
一会船总顺顺从外面回来了，样子沉沉的，这豪爽正直的中年人，正似乎为不幸打倒努力想挣扎爬起的神气，一见到老船夫就说：	A short while later, Fleetmaster Shunshun arrived home, wholly dejected. This honest middle-aged man, ordinarily bold and gregarious, seemed beaten down by his misfortune. Struggling to go forward, he said, as soon as he saw the old ferryman:
「老伯伯，我们谈的那件事情吹了吧。天保大老已经坏了，你知道了吧？」	"Elder Uncle, that plan of ours has fallen through. Tianbao has met his end. Have you heard?"
老船夫两只眼睛红红的，把手搓着，「怎么的，这是真事！是昨天，是前天？」	His eyes red, the old ferryman wrung his hands: "What, so it's true? It can't be! Did it happen yesterday or the day before?"
另一个像是赶路同来报信的，插嘴说道：「十六中上，船搁到石包子上，船头进了水，大老想把篙撇着，人就弹到水中去了。」	Another man broke in, who appeared to be just back with the news: "The morning of the sixteenth, the boat got stuck on a reef and water came pouring over the bow. No. 1 was flipped into the water while trying to pole the boat free."
老船夫说：「你眼见他下水吗？」	The old ferryman asked: "Did you see him fall into the water?"
「我还与他同时下水」	"I fell in with him!"
「他说什么？」	"What did he say?"
「什么都来不及说！这几天来他都不说话」	"He had no time to speak! During the whole trip, he didn't say a word!"
老船夫把头摇摇，向顺顺那么怯怯的溜了一眼。	The old ferryman shook his head and timidly looked at Shunshun.
船总顺顺像知道他心中不安处，就说：「伯伯，一切是天，算了吧。我这里有大兴场人送来的好烧酒，你拿一点去喝罢。」	As if aware of his unease, Fleetmaster Shunshun said, "Uncle, it's all Heaven's doing. That's all there is to it. Someone from Daxingchang has given me a gift of fine wine. Take some home with you."
一个伙计用竹筒上了一筒酒，用新桐木叶蒙着筒口，交给了老船夫。	One of the lads brought a bamboo tube full of wine and covered it with a fresh tung-tree leaf. He gave it to the old ferryman.
老船夫把酒拿走，到了河街后，低头向河码头走去，到河边天保大前天上船处去看看。	Taking the wine, the old ferryman went out onto River Street, then bowed his head and walked toward the wharves to find the place where Tianbao had boarded his boat three days before.
杨马兵还在那里放马到沙地上打滚，自己坐在柳树荫下乘凉。	Horseman Yang was already there, keeping cool in the shade of a willow tree while letting his horse roll around on the sandy shore.
老船夫就走过去请马兵试试那大兴场的烧酒，两人喝了点酒后，兴致似乎皆好些了，老船夫就告给杨马兵，十四夜里二老过碧溪岨唱歌那件事情。	The old ferryman walked over and asked him to taste the wine from Daxingchang.  After a few swallows, when they were in better spirits, the ferryman told Horseman Yang how on the night of the fourteenth the two brothers had come to Green Creek Hill to sing.
那马兵听到后便说：	When Horseman Yang heard this, he said,
「伯伯，你是不是以为翠翠愿意二老应该派归二老－－」	"Uncle, don't you think Cuicui ought to go to No. 2, since she's willing  "
话没说完，傩送二老却从河街下来了。	He hadn't even finished his sentence when Nuosong, No. 2 himself, came down to the river.
这年青人正像要远行的样子，一见了老船夫就回头走去。	The young man looked as if he were about to go on a long trip.  Catching sight of the old ferryman, he averted his gaze and went the other way.
杨马兵就喊他说：「二老，二老，你来，有话同你说呀」	Horseman Yang called out to him, "No. 2, No. 2, over here, I'd like to talk to you!"
二老站定了，很不高兴神气，问马兵「有什么话说」。	No. 2 halted. Irritated, he asked the horseman, "What is it?"
马兵望望老船夫，就向二老说：「你来，有话说」	The horseman looked at the old ferryman, then said to No. 2, "Come here, I've got something to say!"
「什么话？」	"What?"
「我听人说你已经走了－－你过来我同你说，我不会吃掉你」	"I'd heard you'd already gone  come over here so we can talk, I won't bite you! When are you leaving?"
那黑脸宽肩膊，样子虎虎有生气的傩送二老，勉强笑着，到了柳荫下时，老船夫想把空气缓和下来，指着河上游远处那座新碾坊说：「二老，听人说那碾坊将来是归你的！归了你，派我来守碾子，行不行？」	Nuosong, dark-faced, broad-shouldered, and full of life and energy, forced a smile and came over under the willow. Wanting to clear the air, the old ferryman pointed toward the new mill far upriver and said, "No. 2, I hear that mill will be yours in the future! When it is, what say you let me run it for you?"
二老彷佛听不惯这个询问的用意，便不作声。	As if irritated by what the old ferryman was driving at, No. 2 remained silent.
杨马兵看风头有点儿僵，便说：「二老，你怎么的，预备下去吗？」那年青人把头点点，不再说什么，就走开了。	Horseman Yang, seeing that they were headed toward an impasse, put in: "No. 2, how goes it, are you ready to set sail?" The young man nodded. He left without another word.
老船夫讨了个没趣，很懊恼的赶回碧溪岨去，到了渡船上时，就装作把事情看得极随便似的，告给翠翠。	Realizing that he had brought about his own humiliation, the old ferryman returned to Green Creek Hill feeling very upset. When he reached the ferry, he pretended to have taken it all in stride as he told Cuicui:
「翠翠，今天城里出了件新鲜事情，天保大老驾油船下辰州，运气不好，掉到茨滩淹坏了。」	"Cuicui, news has come from the city today. Tianbao, No. 1, took his oil boat downstream to Chenzhou and ran into some bad luck. He met his end in the Puncture Vine Rapids."
翠翠因为听不懂，对于这个报告最先好像全不在意。	Not having understood his meaning, Cuicui at first seemed not to take Grandpa's report too seriously.
祖父又说：	So he added:
「翠翠，这是真事。上次来到这里做保山的杨马兵，还说我早不答应亲事，极有见识」	"It's true, Cuicui. Horseman Yang, who came here the time before as a matchmaker, even said that by not giving you away too soon, I showed a lot of foresight!"
翠翠瞥了祖父一眼，见他眼睛红红的，知道他喝了酒，且有了点事情不高兴，心中想：「谁撩你生气？」	A quick glance at Grandpa told Cuicui that his eyes were red.  She knew he'd been drinking and also that something was troubling him. She thought, "Who got you so angry?"
船到家边时，祖父不自然的笑着向家中走去。	When the ferryboat reached the home side, Grandpa laughed unnaturally and went toward the house.
翠翠守船，半天不闻祖父声息，赶回家去看看，见祖父正坐在门坎上编草鞋耳子。	Cuicui remained in the boat. Hearing nothing from Grandpa for a very long time, she headed home herself to have a look.  She saw Grandpa sitting on the doorstep, plaiting straw sandals.
翠翠见祖父神气极不对，就蹲到他身前去。	She could tell that Grandpa was not himself. She knelt in front of him.
「爷爷，你怎么的？」	"Grandfather, what's bothering you?"
「天保当真死了！二老生了我们的气，以为他家中出这件事情，是我们分派的」	"Tianbao is dead, don't you see. No. 2 is angry at us. He thinks we caused all this."
有人在溪边大声喊渡船过渡，祖父匆匆出去了。	Someone at the stream hailed the ferry, so Grandpa hurried on out.
翠翠坐在那屋角隅稻草上，心中极乱，等等还不见祖父回来，就哭起来了。	Cuicui sat on a pile of rice straw in the corner of the house, greatly upset.  When Grandpa didn't return, she began to cry.
第十七章	CHAPTER SEVENTEEN
祖父似乎生谁的气，脸上笑容减少了，对于翠翠方面也不大注意了。	Grandpa seemed angry at someone.  He didn't smile as much as before, and he didn't pay much attention to Cuicui.
翠翠像知道祖父已不很疼她，但又像不明白它的原因。	She began to realize that Grandpa was not doting on her as usual, yet she seemed not to understand the real reason for it.
但这并不是很久的事，日子一过去，也就好了。	But this didn't last very long.  Things got better as the days passed.
两人仍然划船过日子，一切依旧，惟对于生活，却彷佛什么地方有了个看不见的缺口，始终无法填补起来。	The pair still spent their days on the ferryboat just as always, except that there seemed to be some invisible absence in their lives that simply could not be filled.
祖父过河街去仍然可以得到船总顺顺的款待，但很明显的事，那船总却并不忘掉死去者死亡的原因。	When Grandpa went to River Street, Fleetmaster Shunshun still entertained him as before, yet it was quite apparent that the fleetmaster could never forget why his deceased son had come to be deceased.
二老出北河下辰州走了六百里，沿河找寻那个可怜哥哥的尸骸，毫无结果，在各处税关上贴下招字，返回茶峒来了。	No. 2 had ventured two hundred miles down the White River to Chenzhou, searching for the corpse of his elder brother all along the way.  It was in vain.  After posting notices at all the customs stations, he returned to Chadong.
过不久，他又过川东去办货，过渡时见到老船夫。	Not long after, on his way to transport goods to East Sichuan, he came upon the old ferryman at the crossing.
老船夫看看那小伙子，好像已完全忘掉了从前的事情，就同他说话。	Observing that the young man seemed to have forgotten what had gone before, the old ferryman said to him,
「二老，大六月日头毒人，你又上川东去，不怕辛苦？」	"No. 2, traveling in the heat of the sixth month is terribly punishing, yet here you are on your way to East Sichuan again. I guess you can stand any hardship!"
「要饭吃，头上是火也得上路！」	"We have to eat. I'd have to be on my way even if the heavens above were on fire!"
「要吃饭！二老家还少饭吃！」	"Eat? Don't tell me that's a problem in No. 2's family!"
「有饭吃，爹爹说年青人也不应该在家中白吃不作事！」	"Oh, we have what we need, but Father says that young men ought not to stay home and eat without earning their keep!"
「你爹爹好吗？」	"How is your father these days?"
「吃得做得，有什么不好。」	"He eats and works, as before. Why do you ask?"
「你哥哥坏了，我看你爹爹为这件事情也好像萎悴多了！」二老听到这句话，不作声了，眼睛望着老船夫屋后那个白塔。他似乎想起了过去那个晚上那件旧事，心中十分惆怅。	"Ever since your elder brother's misfortune, the tragedy seems to me to have dealt your father a heavy blow!" No. 2 was silent. He gazed at the white pagoda behind the old ferryman's house, as if recalling, wholly disconsolate, that night from the time before and the events that went with it.
老船夫怯怯的望了年青人一眼，一个微笑在脸上漾开。	The old ferryman stole a fearful glance at the young man and broke out in a smile.
「二老，我家翠翠说，五月里有天晚上，做了个梦－－」说时他又望望二老，见二老并不惊讶，也不厌烦，于是又接着说，「她梦得古怪，说在梦中被一个人的歌声浮起来，上悬岩摘了一把虎耳草！」	"No. 2, my Cuicui tells me that one night during the last month she had a dream  " Watching No. 2 as he spoke, he saw neither shock nor irritation, so he went on: "It was strange. She said that in her dream someone's songs floated her up to the bluffs across the creek, where she picked a handful of saxifrage!"
二老把头偏过一旁去作了一个苦笑，心中想到「老头子倒会做作」。	No. 2 tilted his head and made a wry smile, thinking to himself, "This old codger is up to something."
这点意思在那个苦笑上，彷佛同样泄露出来，仍然被老船夫看到了，老船夫就说：「二老，你不信吗？」	His suspicion was revealed in his smile and noted by the old ferryman, who continued, evidently flustered, "No. 2, don't you believe me?"
那年青人说：「我怎么不相信？因为我做傻子在那边岩上唱过一晚的歌！」	The young man replied: "Why wouldn't I believe you? I was a fool to sing all night long from the top of those cliffs!"
老船夫被一句料想不到的老实话窘住了，口中结结巴巴的说：「这是真的－－这是假的－－」	Shocked and humiliated by this unexpected bluntness, the ferryman stammered: "Really?  Surely not  "
「怎么不是真的？天保大老的死，难道不是真的！」	"Oh no? What about the death of Tianbao? Isn't that real?"
「可是，可是－－」	"But, but  "
老船夫的做作处，原意只是想把事情弄明白一点，但一起始自己叙述这段事情时，方法上就有了错处，因此反被二老误会了。	The old ferryman's pretenses had originally been aimed only at clarifying the situation a little, but from the start he sensed that he had done the wrong thing and been misunderstood.
他这时正想把那夜的情形好好说出来，船已到了岸边。	He wanted now to give a complete explanation of the events of that night, but the boat had reached the other bank.
二老一跃上了岸，就想走去。	No. 2 wanted to be on his way as soon as he jumped to shore.
老船夫在船上显得更加忙乱的样子说：	The old ferryman shouted to him from the boat, all the more flustered:
「二老，二老，你等等，我有话同你说，你先前不是说到那个－－你做傻子的事情吗？你并不傻，别人才当真叫你那歌弄成傻相！」	"No. 2, No. 2, wait up, I have something to tell you. You know that part about you being a fool? You were no fool  it was your counterpart who went into a foolish rapture because of your songs!"
那年青人虽站定了，口中却轻轻的说：「得了够了，不要说了。」	The young man paused a moment, but he said, softly: "That's it. Enough of this. Don't talk about it anymore."
老船夫说：「二老，我听人说你不要碾子要渡船，这是杨马兵说的，不是真的吧？」	The old ferryman continued, "No. 2, I heard that you'd rather tend a ferryboat than a grain mill. Horseman Yang told me so. Was he right?"
那年青人说：「要渡船又怎样？」	The young man said, "And what if I did want the ferryboat?"
老船夫看看二老的神气，心中忽然高兴起来了，就情不自禁的高声叫着翠翠，要她下溪边来。	Suddenly cheered by the look on No. 2's face, the old ferryman couldn't resist loudly shouting for Cuicui to come down to the stream.
可是，不知翠翠是故意不从屋里出来，还是到别处去了，许久还不见到翠翠的影子，也不闻这个女孩子的声音。	But luck was not with him.  He waited a long while and still there was no sign of her, and no response.  She had either gone off or was purposely staying inside the house.
二老等了一会，看看老船夫那副神气，一句话不说，便微笑着，大踏步同一个挑担粉条白糖货物的脚夫走去了。	No. 2 waited for a while in silence, watching the expression on the old ferryman's face, before smiling and striding off with a porter who was bearing loads of bean starch noodles and refined sugar.
过了碧溪岨小山，两人应沿着一条曲曲折折的竹林走去，那个脚夫这时节开了口：	Once they passed the low mountain called Green Creek Hill, the two took a winding path that skirted a bamboo grove. The porter spoke what was on his mind:
「傩送二老，看那弄渡船的神气，很欢喜你！」	"Nuosong, I can tell from his look that this ferryman has really taken a liking to you!"
二老不作声，那人就又说道：	When No. 2 didn't answer, the man said:
「二老，他问你要碾坊还是要渡船，你当真预备做他的孙女婿，接替他那只渡船吗？」	"No. 2, he asked if you preferred the mill or the ferry. Are you really going to marry his granddaughter and take over his beat-up ferryboat?"
二老笑了，那人又说：	No. 2 laughed. The other man went on:
「二老，若这件事派给我，我要那座碾坊。一座碾坊的出息，每天可收七升米，三斗糠。」	"No. 2, if it were my choice, I'd take the grain mill. There's a future in that. It'll make you three pints of rice and ten times that in bran."
二老说：「我回来时向我爹爹去说，为你向中寨人做媒，让你得到那座碾坊吧。	No. 2 responded: "When I get back, I'll put in a word for you with my father. He can make you a match with those people in Middle Stockade, so you can have your mill.
至于我呢，我想弄渡船是很好的。	As for me, I'd be fine with that ferryboat.
只是老家伙为人弯弯曲曲，不利索，大老是他弄死的。」	But the old man is too cunning by far. He's the one who led No. 1 to his demise."
老船夫见二老那么走去了，翠翠还不出来，心中很不快乐。	The old ferryman was disconsolate to see No. 2 go on his way.  Still Cuicui had not come out.
走回家去看看，原来翠翠并不在家。	He went to the house for a look and Cuicui was not there.
过一会，翠翠提了个篮子从小山后回来了，方知道大清早翠翠已出门掘竹鞭笋去了。	A while later, Cuicui emerged from behind a hill, carrying a basket.  He realized that Cuicui had been out all morning, digging up bamboo shoots.
「翠翠，我喊了你好久，你不听到！」	"Cuicui, I called for you for the longest time! You must not have heard."
「喊我做什么？」	"What did you call me for?"
「一个过渡－－一个熟人，我们谈起你－－我喊你你可不答应！」	"There was a passenger on the ferry  someone we know. We got to talking about you. I called you, but you didn't answer!"
「是谁？」	"Who was it?"
「你猜，翠翠。不是陌生人－－你认识他！」	"Guess, Cuicui. He wasn't a stranger, you know him!"
翠翠想起适间从竹林里无意中听来的话，脸红了，半天不说话。	Cuicui thought of the conversation she had inadvertently heard while in the bamboo grove just before. She blushed and for a long time remained quiet.
老船夫问：「翠翠，你得了多少鞭笋？」	The old ferryman asked, "Cuicui, how many bamboo shoots did you gather?"
翠翠把竹篮向地下一倒，除了十来根小小鞭笋外，只是一大把虎耳草。	Cuicui turned her bamboo basket upside down. Besides a dozen or so little bamboo shoots, there was a big clump of saxifrage.
老船夫望了翠翠一眼，翠翠两颊绯红跑了。	The old ferryman shot her a glance. Her cheeks flushing scarlet, Cuicui hurried away.
第十八章	CHAPTER EIGHTEEN
日子平平的过了一个月，一切人心上的病痛，似乎皆在那份长长的白日下医治好了。	As another month passed quietly by, the heartaches of all concerned seemed cured by the long summer days.
天气特别热，各人只忙着流汗，用凉水淘江米酒吃，不用什么心事，心事在人生活中，也就留不住了。	The weather grew so hot that everyone was preoccupied with their sweating and they ate their fermented glutinous rice in cold water.  There was no place left in their lives for heartaches and worries.
翠翠每天皆到白塔下背太阳的一面去午睡，高处既极凉快，两山竹篁里叫得使人发松的竹雀和其它鸟类又如此之多，致使她在睡梦里尽为山鸟歌声所浮着，做的梦也便常是顶荒唐的梦。	Every afternoon, Cuicui took a nap on the shady side of the pagoda.  It was very cool on that elevated spot.  The soothing songs of bamboo finches and other birds came from the bamboo stands of the mountains on either side. The birds were such a numerous flock that in her dreams the mountain birdsong lifted her up into the air and brought her the most fantastic dreams.
这并不是人的罪过。	There was no sin in that.
诗人们会在一件小事上写出整本整部的诗，雕刻家在一块石头上雕得出骨血如生的人像，画家一撇儿绿，一撇儿红，一撇儿灰，画得出一幅一幅带有魔力的彩画，谁不是为了惦着一个微笑的影子，或是一个皱眉的记号，方弄出那么些古怪成绩？	Poets could spin out books of poetry from a small incident.  Sculptors could carve the living image of a person in a piece of stone, and painters could turn out one magical painting after another from streaks of green, red, and gray.  Who among them was not inspired by the memory of a smile, or a frown?
翠翠不能用文字，不能用石头，不能用颜色把那点心头上的爱憎移到别一件东西上去，却只让她的心，在一切顶荒唐事情上驰骋。	Cuicui could not use writing, or stone, or colors, to transfer her heart's passions of love and hate into a work of art, she could only let her heart race ahead with the most absurd thoughts.
她从这分隐秘里，常常得到又惊又喜的兴奋。	This secretiveness often brought her an excitement both shocking and elating.
一点儿不可知的未来，摇撼她的情感极厉害，她无从完全把那种痴处不让祖父知道。	A wholly unknowable future was shaking her emotions to their foundations, and she could not completely hide these passions from her grandpa.
祖父呢，可以说一切都知道了的。但事实上他又却是个一无所知的人。	As to Grandpa, one could say that he knew everything, but in fact he was wholly ignorant.
他明白翠翠不讨厌那个二老，却不明白那小伙子二老怎么样。	He understood that Cuicui was not displeased with the No. 2 son, but he could not comprehend the young man's own disposition.
他从船总处与二老处，皆碰过了钉子，但他并不灰心。	He had met with rebuffs from both the fleetmaster and No. 2, yet he failed to be discouraged.
「要安排得对一点，方合道理，一切有个命」他那么想着，就更显得好事多磨起来了。睁着眼睛时，他做的梦比那个外孙女翠翠便更荒唐更寥阔。	"If I can fix things up a little better, it will turn out all right, if only fate allows!" In that frame of mind, he mused that the course of love was never easy. The visions he dreamed with his eyes wide open were even more fantastic and unfettered than those of his granddaughter, Cuicui.
他向各个过渡本地人打听二老父子的生活，关切他们如同自己家中人一样。	He inquired about the lives of No. 2 and his father from every local person who took his ferry, as solicitous about the River Street people as if they were family.
但也古怪，因此他却怕见到那个船总同二老了。	Yet, strangely enough, this made him all the more fearful of actually running into them.
一见他们他就不知说些什么，只是老脾气把两只手搓来搓去，从容处完全失去了。	When he did, he couldn't think of a thing to say.  He rubbed his hands together nervously, as was his habit, having completely lost his composure.
二老父子方面皆明白他的意思，但那个死去的人，却用一个凄凉的印象，镶嵌到父子心中，两人便对于老船夫的意思，俨然全不明白似的，一同把日子打发下去。	No. 2 and his father knew what he was up to, but the departed son, to use a cold expression, was chiseled into their hearts.  They went about their business as the days passed by, acting as if they didn't know what the old ferryman was about.
明明白白夜来并不作梦，早晨同翠翠说话时，那作祖父的会说：	Early in the morning, when it was obvious that he had not dreamed a single dream the night before, Grandpa would say,
「翠翠，翠翠，我昨晚上做了个好不怕人的梦」	"Cuicui, Cuicui, last night I had a simply awful dream."
翠翠问：「什么怕人的梦？」	"What awful dream?" Cuicui asked.
就装作思索梦境似的，一面细看翠翠小脸长眉毛，一面说出他另一时张着眼睛所做的好梦。	Then, pretending to be remembering his dream, he would scrutinize Cuicui's slender face and long eyebrows while telling her of a wonderful daydream he'd imagined at another time.
不消说，那些梦原来都并不是当真怎样使人吓怕的。	Needless to say, none of these dreams were so fearsome after all.
一切河流皆得归海，话起始说得纵极远，到头来总仍然是归到使翠翠红脸那件事情上去。	All streams flow to the sea eventually.  Although the conversation took a quite different direction to start, in the end it always came back to those matters that made Cuicui blush.
待到翠翠显得不大高兴，神气上露出受了点小窘时，这老船夫又才像有了一点儿吓怕，忙着解释，用闲话来遮掩自己所说到那问题的原意。	Only when it became evident that Cuicui was displeased, her expression betraying embarrassment, did the old ferryman pretend that he was upset and hurry to explain himself, using small talk to cover up his intentions in bringing up these matters.
「翠翠，我不是那么说，我不是那么说。爷爷老了，胡涂了，笑话多咧。」	"Cuicui, that's not what I meant, not at all. Your grandfather is old and muddled, full of crazy talk."
但有时翠翠却静静的把祖父那些笑话胡涂话听下去，一直听到后来还抿着嘴儿微笑。	But sometimes Cuicui quietly listened to Grandpa's crazy talk and muddled thoughts, to the point where she found herself smiling to herself.
翠翠也会忽然说道：	She might suddenly blurt out:
「爷爷，你真是有一点儿胡涂」	"Grandfather, you really are mixed up!"
祖父听过了不再作声，他将说，「我有一大堆心事，」但来不及说，恰好就被过渡人喊走了。	Hearing that, Grandpa would stop speaking. He meant to go on to say, "There are a lot of things on my mind," but before he could speak, he was summoned by a ferry passenger.
天气热了，过渡人从远处走来，肩上挑得是七十斤担子，到了溪边，贪凉快不即走路，必蹲在岩石下茶缸边喝凉茶，与同伴交换「吹吹棒」烟管，且一面与弄渡船的攀谈。	It was hot, so when ferry passengers from far away arrived bearing eighty-pound loads on their shoulder poles, they would rest and cool off by the creek.
许多子虚乌有的话皆从此说出口来，给老船夫听到了。	Squatting under the cliffs by the keg to enjoy a cool drink of tea, they passed their long "puffer" tobacco pipe between them while drawing the ferryman into their conversation. Thus did all sorts of baseless rumors, from the heavens above to the earth below, reach the old ferryman's ears.
过渡人有时还因溪水清洁，就溪边洗脚抹澡的，坐得更久话也就更多。	Sometimes the passengers would take advantage of the clean stream waters to wash their feet or bathe. The longer they stayed, the more gossip passed between them.
祖父把些话转说给翠翠，翠翠也就学懂了许多事情。货物的价钱涨落呀，坐轿搭船的用费呀，放木筏的人把他那个木筏从滩上流下时，十来把大桡子如何活动呀，在小烟船上吃荤烟，大脚娘如何烧烟呀－－无一不备。	Grandpa passed some of the talk on to Cuicui, and she learned a good deal in the process: the rise and fall of commodity prices, the going rate for riding a sedan chair or a boat, how to steer a timber raft down the rapids using its rudders, what it was like to look for a prostitute on an opium sampan, how ladies of the night with unbound feet boiled the opium  just about everything.
傩送二老从川东押物回到了茶峒。	Nuosong, No. 2, returned to Chadong with his goods from East Sichuan.
时间已近黄昏了，溪面很寂静，祖父同翠翠在菜园地里看萝卜秧子。	It was almost dusk and very still out on the stream.  Grandpa and Cuicui were in the vegetable garden, inspecting the turnip sprouts.
翠翠白日中觉睡久了些，觉得有点寂寞，好像听人嘶声喊过渡，就争先走下溪边去。	Cuicui had napped a little too long that day and was feeling a little forlorn, so when she thought she heard a hoarse voice summon the ferry, she was the first to go down to the landing.
下坎时，见两个人站在码头边，斜阳影里背身看得极分明，正是傩送二老同他家中的长年！	As she went down the bank, she saw two men standing by the pier.  She could recognize them clearly in the light of the setting sun, though their backs were to her: it was Nuosong, No. 2, and the family servant!
翠翠大吃一惊，同小兽物见到猎人一样，回头便向山竹林里跑掉了。	Startled, like a little wild animal encountering a hunter, Cuicui ran back into the bamboo grove on the hill.
但那两个在溪边的人，听到脚步响时，一转身，也就看明白这件事情了。	But the two men at the stream turned around at the sound of her footfall and saw everything.
等了一下再也不见人来，那长年又嘶声音喊叫过渡。	They waited a while and still no one came, so the servant shouted again for the ferry in his raspy voice.
老船夫听得清清楚楚，却仍然蹲在萝卜秧地上数菜，心里觉得好笑。	The old ferryman heard him very clearly, but continued squatting in the garden, counting his turnip sprouts. He found it amusing.
他已见到翠翠走去，他知道必是翠翠看明白了过渡人是谁，故蹲在那高岩上不理会。	He'd seen Cuicui take flight and knew it must be because she recognized someone at the landing.  He purposely kept on squatting under the high cliffs, ignoring the men.
翠翠人小不管事，过渡人求她不干，奈何她不得，故只好嘶着个喉咙叫过渡了。	Cuicui was young and not in charge; when she didn't respond to the men who wanted to cross, they had no recourse but to keep straining their voices to summon the ferry.
那长年叫了几声，见无人来，就停了，同二老说：「这是什么玩意儿，难道老的害病弄翻了，只剩下翠翠一个人了吗？」二老说：「等等看，不算什么」就等了一阵。因为这边在静静的等着，园地上老船夫却在心里想：「难道是二老吗？」他彷佛担心搅恼了翠翠似的，就仍然蹲着不动。	After several more shouts, the hired man rested his tired voice and asked No. 2, "What's this all about? You don't suppose the old man is down sick and has left the ferry to Cuicui all by herself?" No. 2 answered, "Let's wait, we're in no hurry!" So they waited awhile. Because the passengers had fallen quiet, the old ferryman in the garden thought to himself: "Could it be No. 2?" As if afraid of annoying Cuicui further, he kept on squatting there and didn't make a move.
但再过一阵，溪边又喊起过渡来了，声音不同了一点，这才真是二老的声音。	But not long after, the shouting for the ferry resumed, and this time it sounded a little different.  It was No. 2's voice.
生气了吧？	Was he angry?
等久了吧？	Tired of waiting?
吵嘴了吧？	Had there been an argument?
老船夫一面胡乱估着一面跑到溪边去。	Frantically trying to size up the situation, the old ferryman raced down to the stream bank.
到了溪边，见两个人业已上了船，其中之一正是二老。	When he got there, he saw the two men already aboard the boat, and one of them was No. 2.
老船夫惊讶的喊叫：	The old ferryman shouted out, anxiously,
「呀，二老，你回来了」	"Hey there, No. 2, you're back!"
年青人很不高兴似的，「回来了。－－你们这渡船是怎么的，等了半天也不来个人」	Showing his displeasure, the young man answered, "Yes, I'm back. What's wrong with you folks at the ferry? We waited forever and no one came for us!"
「我以为－－」老船夫四处一望，并不见翠翠的影子，只见黄狗从山上竹林里跑来，知道翠翠上山了，便改口说，「我以为你们过了渡。」	"I thought it was  " he looked all around and there was no trace of Cuicui, but just then the yellow dog ran out of the bamboo grove on the mountain, so he knew she had gone up there. He changed his drift and said: "I thought you had already crossed over."
「过了渡！不得你上船，谁敢开船？」那长年说着，一只水鸟掠着水面飞去，「翠鸟儿归窠了，我们还得赶回家去吃夜饭」	"Already crossed over? Who would dare launch the boat without you?" said the servant. As he spoke, a waterfowl skimmed over the water. "That jade-green bird is headed toward its nest. We have to hurry back home in time for supper!"
「早咧，到河街早咧，」说着，老船夫已跳上了船，且在心中一面说着，「你不是想承继这只渡船吗」一面把船索拉动，船便离岸了。	"You're in time, you've got plenty of time to get to River Street." The old ferryman had already jumped into the boat. "Don't you want to inherit this ferryboat for your own?" he thought, as he pulled on the cable and the boat left the shore.
「二老，路上累得很！－－」	"No. 2, it must have been a tiring trip!"
老船夫说着，二老不置可否不动感情听下去。	As the old ferryman spoke, No. 2 listened without letting on how he was feeling.
船拢了岸，那年青小伙子同家中长年挑担子翻山走了。	When they reached the shore, the young man and his servant shouldered their loads and crossed over the hill without saying a word.
那点淡漠印象留在老船夫心上，老船夫于是在两个人身后，捏紧拳头威吓了三下，轻轻的吼着，把船拉回去了。	The old ferryman took note of their coolness.  He shook his fist at them behind their backs, shook it three times.  He cursed them under his breath and pulled the boat back to his side.
第十九章	CHAPTER NINETEEN
翠翠向竹林里跑去，老船夫半天还不下船，这件事从傩送二老看来，前途显然有点不利。	Cuicui's flight into the bamboo grove and the old ferryman's long delay in coming down to the landing suggested to Nuosong that his prospects here were not good.
虽老船夫言词之间，无一句话不在说明「这事有边」，但那畏畏缩缩的说明，极不得体，二老想起他的哥哥，便把这件事曲解了。	Although the old ferryman was constantly intimating that Nuosong "had a chance for success in this," the old man's hesitant explanations were very inept; they made No. 2 think of his elder brother, and he misinterpreted them.
他有一点愤愤不平，有一点儿气恼。	He felt a little aggrieved and a little angry.
回到家里第三天，中寨有人来探口风，在河街顺顺家中住下，把话问及顺顺，想明白二老是不是还有意接受那座新碾坊，顺顺就转问二老自己意见怎么样。	On his third day back home, someone arrived from Middle Stockade to sound him out.  During an overnight stay in Shunshun's house on River Street, the man asked Shunshun where No. 2 stood  did he still want the new mill or not?  Shunshun referred the question to No. 2 himself.
二老说：「爸爸，你以为这事为你，家中多座碾坊多个人，你可以快活，你就答应了。	No. 2 answered, "Papa, if this is for you  if adding a mill and a woman to the household would make you happy, then you give the go-ahead.
若果为的是我，我要好好去想一下，过些日子再说它吧。	If this is for me, then I need to think it over and wait a few days before answering.
我还不知道我应当得座碾坊，还是应当得一只渡船：我命里或只许我撑个渡船！」	I still don't know if I ought to take the mill or the ferryboat; perhaps my fate will only allow me to operate the boat!"
探口风的人把话记住，回中寨去报命，到碧溪岨过渡时，到了老船夫，想起二老说的话，不由得不咪咪的笑着。	The man who'd come to sound them out marked these words and set out for Middle Stockade to report on his mission.  When he came to the ferry at Green Creek Hill and saw the old ferryman, he recalled No. 2's words and couldn't help smiling to himself.
老船夫问明白了他是中寨人，就又问他过茶峒作什么事。	On learning that the man was from Middle Stockade, the ferryman asked him what business he had in town.
那心中有分寸的中寨人说：	The Middle Stockade man knew enough to be circumspect in his words:
「什么事也不作，只是过河街船总顺顺家里坐了一会儿。」	"Nothing much, I just went to Fleetmaster Shunshun's house on River Street and sat a spell."
「无事不登三宝殿，坐了一定就有话说！」	"They say one doesn't go to the Temple of the Three Buddhist Treasures without a good reason. If you sat down there you must have had something to say!"
「话倒说了几句。」	"We did exchange some pleasantries."
「说了些什么话？」那人不再说了，老船夫却问道，「听说你们中寨人想把大河边一座碾坊连同家中闺女送给河街上顺顺，这事情有不有了点眉目？」	"What did you talk about?" The other man said nothing further, so the old ferryman went on: "I hear that someone from Middle Stockade wants to give away a mill by the riverside, together with his daughter, to Shunshun down on River Street. Has there been any progress in that matter?"
那中寨人笑了，「事情成了。我问过顺顺，顺顺很愿意同中寨人结亲家，又问过那小伙子－－」	The man from Middle Stockade grinned. "It's a done deal. I asked Shunshun. He's quite willing to join families with the man from Middle Stockade.  Then he asked the young man  "
「小伙子意思怎么样？」	"And how did he feel about it?"
「他说：我眼前有座碾坊，有条渡船，我本想要渡船，现在就决定要碾坊吧。	"He said: 'A mill and a ferryboat lie before me. Originally I wanted the ferry, but now I've decided on the mill.
渡船是活动的，不如碾坊固定。	A boat is always on the move, whereas a mill stays in place.'
这小子会打算盘呢。」	That fellow has a head on him."
中寨人是个米场经纪人，话说得极有斤两，他明知道「渡船」指的是什么，但他可并不说穿。	This man from Middle Stockade was a rice broker, good at weighing his words. He well knew what the "ferryboat" referred to, but he didn't let on.
他看到老船夫口唇蠕动，想要说话，中寨人便又抢着说道：	When he saw the old ferryman start to speak, the Middle Stockade man broke in first:
「一切皆是命，半点不由人。可怜顺顺家那个大老，相貌一表堂堂，会淹死在水里！」	"Everything depends on fate. Human actions hardly have a hand in it. It's too bad that Shunshun's No. 1  such a handsome lad  had to drown in the river!"
老船夫被这句话在心上戳了一下，把想问的话咽住了。	This stabbed the old ferryman right in the heart.  He swallowed the words he was about to speak.
中寨人上岸走去后，老船夫闷闷的立在船头，痴了许久。	After the man from Middle Stockade had come ashore and gone on his way, the old ferryman stood dejectedly in the prow of his boat, dazed.
又把二老日前过渡时落寞神气温习一番，心中大不快乐。	Ruminating about how distant No. 2 had been the time before, he felt very upset.
翠翠在塔下玩得极高兴，走到溪边高岩上想要祖父唱唱歌，见祖父不理会她，一路埋怨赶下溪边去，到了溪边方见到祖父神气十分沮丧，不明白为什么原因。	Cuicui was quite happily occupied under the pagoda.  She went up to the high bluffs, wanting Grandpa to sing to her from below, but he paid her no attention.  She went down to the stream, sulking, until she saw that Grandpa for some unknown reason looked very dispirited.
翠翠来了，祖父看看翠翠的快活黑脸儿，粗卤的笑笑。	When Cuicui approached and Grandpa saw her dusky, happy face, he put on a semblance of a smile.
对溪有扛货物过渡的，便不说什么，沉默的把船拉过溪，到了中心却大声唱起歌来了。	But there was someone transporting goods awaiting the ferry on the other side, so Grandpa said nothing.  He pulled the boat south across the stream in silence, until midway he broke out loudly into song.
把人渡了过溪，祖父跳上码头走近翠翠身边来，还是那么粗卤的笑着，把手抚着头额。	After ferrying the passenger, Grandpa jumped up on the dock and went up to Cuicui with a wry smile on his face again.  He wiped his forehead with his hand.
翠翠说：	Cuicui said,
「爷爷怎么的，你发痧了？你躺到荫下去歇歇，我来管船！」	"What's the matter, Grandfather, are you suffering from heatstroke? Lie down and rest in the shade! I'll take care of the boat."
「你来管船，好，这只船归你管！」	"Yes, you take care of it. Fine. Excellent, this boat is yours to take care of!"
老船夫似乎当真发了痧，心头发闷，虽当着翠翠还显出硬扎样子，独自走回屋里后，找寻得到一些碎瓷片，在自己臂上腿上扎了几下，放出了些乌血，就躺到床上睡了。	He felt like he really did have heatstroke. He was sick at heart. Though he put up a strong front before Cuicui, when he was alone in the house he found a piece of broken porcelain, cut himself in a few places on his arms and legs to let out some blood, then lay down to sleep.
翠翠自己守船，心中却古怪的快乐，心想：「爷爷不为我唱歌，我自己会唱！」	Taking up her post on the boat, Cuicui felt strangely euphoric. She thought: "If Grandfather won't sing for me, I'll sing myself."
她唱了许多歌，老船夫躺在床上闭着眼睛，一句一句听下去，心中极乱。	She sang a good many songs.  Lying in bed with his eyes shut and listening closely, the old ferryman grew anxious.
但他知道这不是能够把他打倒的大病，他明天就仍然会爬起来的。	But he knew that this illness would not be the end of him; he would still be able to get up tomorrow.
他想明天进城，到河街去看看，又想起许多旁的事情。	He decided to go to town the next day and look around on River Street.  He also mulled over many other matters.
但到了第二天，人虽起了床，头还沉沉的。	When the morning came, however, though he left the bed, his head still hung heavy.
祖父当真已病了。	Grandpa was truly ill.
翠翠显得懂事了些，为祖父煎了一罐大发药，逼着祖父喝，又在屋后菜园地里摘取蒜苗泡在米汤里作酸蒜苗。	Cuicui, knowing just what to do, boiled up a pot of fever-breaking herbal medicine and made Grandpa drink it.  She also went out back to the garden to pick sour garlic sprouts for steeping in rice broth, as a cure.
一面照料船只，一面还时时刻刻抽空赶回家里来看祖父，问这样那样。	She frequently took time out from minding the boat to return home and look in on Grandpa and ply him with questions.
祖父可不说什么，只是为一个秘密痛苦着。	But he had nothing to say; a secret pained him.
躺了三天，人居然好了。	Yet, after three days in bed, he was well.
屋前屋后走动了一下，骨头还硬硬的，心中惦念到一件事情，便预备进城过河街去。	He seemed strong as ever as he paced in front and back of the house, but something was worrying him, so he prepared to journey to River Street.
翠翠看不出祖父有什么要紧事情必须当天进城，请求他莫去。	Cuicui couldn't understand what could be so important as to make Grandpa go to town so soon.  She begged him not to go.
老船夫把手搓着，估量到是不是应说出那个理由。	The old ferryman rubbed his hands together, wondering whether he ought to tell her what his business was.
翠翠一张黑黑的瓜子脸，一双水汪汪的眼睛，使他吁了一口气。	Standing before Cuicui, with her bright eyes and dark, oval face, he had to sigh.
他说：「我有要紧事情，得今天去！」	"I have something important to do," he said, "and I have to go today!"
翠翠苦笑着说：「有多大要紧事情，还不是－－」	Cuicui smiled disdainfully: "What's so urgent? Surely it's not  "
老船夫知道翠翠脾气，听翠翠口气已有点不高兴，不再说要走了，把预备带走的竹筒，同扣花褡裢搁到条几上后，带点儿谄媚笑着说：「不去吧，你担心我会摔死，我就不去吧。	The old ferryman knew his granddaughter's temper; he could hear the unhappiness in her voice, so he stopped insisting on going. Laying on the table the bamboo tube and embroidered cloth shoulder bag he'd prepared for the trip, he said, with a fawning smile, "All right, I won't go. Since you're afraid I might fall down dead, I won't go.
我以为早上天气不很热，到城里把事办完了就回来－－不去也得，我明天去！」	I thought I'd go to town in the morning, before it got too hot, and finish my business  but I don't have to go. I can go tomorrow!"
翠翠轻声的温柔的说：「你明天去也好，你腿还软，好好的躺一天再起来。」	Cuicui replied, softly and gently, "Yes, tomorrow will be fine. Your legs are still weak! A day's rest will do you good."
老船夫似乎心中还不甘服，洒着两手走出去，门限边一个打草鞋的棒槌，差点儿把他绊了一大跤。稳住了时翠翠苦笑着说：「爷爷，你瞧，还不服气！」	Seeming not really willing to give in, the old ferryman shrugged and stepped away.  As he crossed over the high door threshold, he nearly tripped headlong over the stick he used to make straw sandals. When he'd steadied himself, Cuicui put on a pained smile and said: "Grandfather, you see, you still don't know how to take advice!"
老船夫拾起那棒槌，向屋角隅摔去，说道：「爷爷老了！过几天打豹子给你看！」	The old man picked up the stick and threw it into a corner of the room, adding: "Your grandfather may be old, but just wait a few days, and I'll hunt you a leopard!"
到了午后，落了一阵行雨，老船夫却同翠翠好好商量，仍然进了城。	In the afternoon it rained, but the old ferryman said good-bye to Cuicui and went to town anyway.
翠翠不能陪祖父进城，就要黄狗跟去。	Since Cuicui couldn't go with him, she insisted that the yellow dog accompany him.
老船夫在城里被一个熟人拉着谈了许久的盐价米价，又过守备衙门看了一会新买的骡马，才到河街顺顺家里去。	Once in town, he was detained by a friend who wanted to talk about the price of salt and rice.  Then he went to the army barracks to see the new mules and horses purchased by the head of the likin tax bureau before he finally got to Shunshun's house on River Street.
到了那里，见到顺顺正同三个人打纸牌，不便谈话，就站在身后看了一阵牌，后来顺顺请他喝酒，借口病刚好点不敢喝酒，推辞了。	There he found Shunshun playing cards with three other men.  Unable to speak to him in private, he just stood behind Shunshun and looked at his hand.  After a while Shunshun invited him for a drink, but the ferryman begged off, on the excuse that he had been sick.
牌既不散场，老船夫又不想即走，顺顺似乎并不明白他等着有何话说，却只注意手中的牌。	The card players weren't ready to go home and the old ferryman wasn't about to leave, either.  Shunshun seemed unable to figure out why he had come; he just concentrated on his hand.
后来老船夫的神气倒为另外一个人看出了，就问他是不是有什么事情。	It was another man who took note of the old ferryman's discomfort and asked if he had something to discuss.
老船夫方忸忸怩怩照老方子搓着他那两只大手，说别的事没有，只想同船总说两句话。	That made the old ferryman rub his two hands together nervously, as was his habit, and say, not really, he just wanted to exchange a word or two with the fleetmaster.
那船总方明白在看牌半天的理由，回头对老船夫笑将起来。	The fleetmaster finally understood why the ferryman had been standing behind him, looking at his cards for so long. He turned around and smiled at the old ferryman.
「怎不早说？你不说，我还以为你在看我牌学张子！」	"Why didn't you say so? You didn't say anything, so I thought you must be trying to learn a few tricks of the game."
「没有什么，只是三五句话，我不便扫兴，不敢说出。」船总把牌向桌上一撒，笑着向后房走去了，老船夫跟在身后。	"It's nothing, just a little something I wanted to talk about. I didn't want to spoil the fun  didn't dare interrupt you." The fleetmaster threw his cards down on the table. Smiling, he went into the back room, with the old ferryman following behind.
「什么事？」船总问着，神气似乎先就明白了他来此要说的话，显得略微有点儿怜悯的样子。	"What's on your mind?" the fleetmaster asked, with an expression hinting that he knew what the boatman was about to say, and also bearing a touch of pity.
「我听一个中寨人说，你预备同中寨团总打亲家，是不是真事？」	"I heard a man from Middle Stockade say you were preparing to link your family in marriage with the militia captain there. Is it true?"
船总见老船夫的眼睛盯着他的脸，想得一个满意的回答，就说：「有这事情。」	The fleetmaster could see the old ferryman's eyes fixed on him, begging for the answer he wanted. "You've heard right," said the fleetmaster.
那么答应，意思却是：「有了你怎么样？」	But the implication was, "What's it to you?"
老船夫说：「真的吗？」	"That's a fact?" the old ferryman asked.
那一个又很自然的说：「真的。」意思却依旧包含了「真的又怎么样？」	"True enough," the other said, unconcernedly. But the implication, again, was another question: "Fact is, what business is it of yours?"
老船夫装得很从容的问：「二老呢？」	Pretending to be completely unruffled, the old ferryman asked, "What does No. 2 say?"
船总说：「二老坐船下桃源好些日子了！」	The fleetmaster replied: "No. 2 has taken a boat down to Taoyuan and been gone for several days now!"
二老下桃源的事，原来还同他爸爸吵了一阵才走的。	As it happened, No. 2 had gone downriver to Taoyuan only after quarreling with his father.
船总性情虽异常豪爽，可不愿意间接把第一个儿子弄死的女孩子，又来作第二个儿子的媳妇，这是很明白的事情。	The fleetmaster might be extremely open-minded, but that didn't mean he was willing to have the girl who had killed his first son, even if indirectly, become the wife of his second; that was very clear.
若照当地风气，这些事认为只是小孩子的事，大人管不着，二老当真欢喜翠翠，翠翠又爱二老，他也并不反对这种爱怨纠缠的婚姻。	Local custom held that these things were all up to the younger generation  the elders were not to interfere.  No. 2 was truly fond of Cuicui, and Cuicui loved No. 2 also.  The fleetmaster was not opposed to this sort of love match.
但不知怎么的，老船夫对于这件事的关心，使二老父子对于老船夫反而有了一点误会。	But for some reason, the old ferryman's concentration on the matter had made both father and son misunderstand his motives.
船总想起家庭间的近事，以为全与这老而好事的船夫有关。	Whenever the fleetmaster thought of his recent family tragedy, he associated it with this old and meddlesome boatman.
虽不见诸形色，心中却有个疙瘩。	There was no outward sign of it, but inwardly there was a big hitch.
船总不让老船夫再开口了，就语气略粗的说道：	Without letting the old ferryman continue, the fleetmaster told him, somewhat bluntly:
「伯伯，算了吧，我们的口只应当喝酒了，莫再只想替儿女唱歌！	"Uncle, no more of this. Our mouths are for drinking, not singing the young folks' songs for them!
你的意思我全明白，你是好意。	I know exactly what you mean to say, and you mean well.
可是我也求你明白我的意思，我以为我们只应当谈点自己分上的事情，不适宜于想那些年青人的门路了。」	But I'm asking you to understand my position. We should talk about matters that are up to us, not try to pull strings for our youngsters."
老船夫被一个闷拳打倒后，还想说两句话，但船总却不让他再有说话机会，把他拉出到牌桌边去。	After this final blow, the old ferryman still had something to say, but the fleetmaster wouldn't let him speak another word; he pulled him back to the card table.
老船夫无话可说，看看船总时，船总虽还笑着谈到许多笑话，心中却似乎很沉郁，把牌用力掷到桌上去。	The old ferryman was speechless.  He looked at the fleetmaster, who was smiling and telling lots of jokes, but the way he threw down his cards showed his distress.
老船夫不说什么，戴起他那个斗笠，自己走了。	Without another word, the old ferryman donned his conical hat and left.
天气还早，老船夫心中很不高兴，又进城去找杨马兵。	It was still early, so the dejected old man went back into town to find Horseman Yang.
那马兵正在喝酒，老船夫虽推病，也免不了喝个三五杯。	He was drinking.  The old ferryman pleaded that he was still sick, but couldn't help drinking a few cups of liquor anyway.
回到碧溪岨，走得热了一点，又用溪水去抹身子。	Feeling hot from the walking by the time he got to Green Creek Hill, he washed himself in the stream.
觉得很疲倦，就要翠翠守船，自己回家睡去了。	He was tired, so he asked Cuicui to keep on tending the boat while he went home and slept.
黄昏时天气十分郁闷，溪面各处飞着红蜻蜓。	As dusk fell, the weather became quite oppressive.  The stream was covered with red dragonflies.
天上已起了云，热风把两山竹篁吹得声音极大，看样子到晚上必落大雨。	Mist was already gathering and hot winds were noisily rustling the bamboos in the mountain groves on either side of the stream.  It looked as if it would rain that night.
翠翠守在渡船上，看着那些溪面飞来飞去的蜻蜓，心也极乱。	Cuicui was with the boat, watching the dragonflies as they flitted across the creek.  Her heart was ill at ease, too.
看祖父脸上颜色惨惨的，放心不下，便又赶回家中去。	Seeing Grandpa so dejected, she grew worried and hurried home.
先以为祖父一定早睡了，谁知还坐在门限上打草鞋！	She thought he would already be in bed, but he was sitting on the doorstep, weaving straw sandals!
「爷爷，你要多少双草鞋，床头上不是还有十四双吗？怎么不好好的躺一躺？」	"Grandfather, how many shoes do you need? Aren't there fourteen pairs up by your bed as it is? Why don't you lie down and rest?"
老船夫不作声，却站起身来昂头向天空望着，轻轻的说：	Instead of answering, the old ferryman stood up and looked at the sky. He said, softly:
「翠翠，今晚上要落大雨响大雷的！回头把我们的船系到岩下去，这雨大哩。」	"Cuicui, there'll be a heavy thunderstorm tonight! Let's tie up our boat under the cliffs. The rain tonight is going to be heavy."
翠翠说：「爷爷，我真吓怕！」翠翠怕的似乎并不是晚上要来的雷雨。	Cuicui said, "Grandfather, I'm afraid!" But what Cuicui feared didn't seem to be the coming thunderstorm.
老船夫似乎也懂得那个意思，就说：「怕什么？一切要来的都得来，不必怕！」	Acting as if he hadn't understood her, the old ferryman said, "What's there to be afraid of? What will be will be. Don't be scared."
第二十章	CHAPTER TWENTY
夜间果然落了大雨，夹以吓人的雷声。	The night did bring a great storm, accompanied by frightening thunderclaps.
电光从屋脊上掠过时，接着就是訇的一个炸电。	Lightning swept over the rooftop, followed by a deafening crash of thunder.
翠翠在暗中抖着。	Cuicui quivered in the dark.
祖父也醒了，知道她害怕，且担心她着凉，还起身来把一条布单搭到她身上去。	Grandpa woke up, too.  Sensing her fear, and worried that she might catch cold, he got up to cover her with a sheet.
祖父说：	Grandpa said:
「翠翠，不要怕」	"Cuicui, don't be afraid!
翠翠说：「我不怕」说了还想说：「爷爷你在这里我不怕」訇的一个大雷，接着是一种超越雨声而上的洪大闷重倾圮声。	Cuicui replied, "I'm not." Meanwhile she thought to herself: "Grandfather, I'm not afraid because you're here!" There came another roll of thunder, and then, overpowering the sound of the rain, the deadening sound of something giving way.
两人都以为一定是溪岸悬崖崩塌了，担心到那只渡船会压在崖石下面去了。	Both of them were sure that the hanging cliffs by the stream bank must have caved in!  They feared that their boat was crushed under collapsing rocks from the cliffs.
祖孙两人便默默的躺在床上听雨声雷声。	Grandfather and granddaughter kept silent in their beds, listening to the sound of the rain and thunder.
但无论如何大雨，过不久，翠翠却依然睡着了。	Even with the downpour, Cuicui was soon asleep again.
醒来时天已亮了，雨不知在何时业已止息，只听到溪两岸山沟里注水入溪的声音。	When she woke up, it was already daylight.  The rain had stopped without her noticing.  She heard only the sound of torrents from the gullies entering the stream from the mountains on both sides.  Cuicui got up out of bed.
翠翠爬起身来，看看祖父还似乎睡得很好，开了门走出去。	Seeing Grandpa still sound asleep, she opened the door and went out.
门前已成为一个水沟，一股水便从塔后哗哗的流来，从前面悬崖直堕而下。	The ground in front of the house had become a ditch and water splashed past in a muddy stream from behind the pagoda, having come straight down from the bluffs.
并且各处都是那么一种临时的水道。	Newly formed channels of water were everywhere.
屋旁菜园地已为山水冲乱了，菜秧皆掩在粗砂泥里了。	The vegetable garden was flooded, its sprouts all covered with sand and gravel.
再走过前面去看看溪里，才知道溪中也涨了大水，已漫过了码头，水脚快到茶缸边了。	Going over to the stream, she could see that the water had risen so high that it was already brimming over the dock.  Soon it would reach the tea vat.
下到码头去的那条路，正同一条小河一样，哗哗的泄着黄泥水。	The path down to the dock was like a little river, splashing yellow mud.
过渡的那一条横溪牵定的缆绳，也被水淹没了，泊在崖下的渡船，已不见了。	The cable over the stream used to pull the boat across was already under water, and the ferryboat, previously tied up beneath the cliffs, was nowhere to be found.
翠翠看看屋前悬崖并不崩坍，故当时还不注意渡船的失去。	Observing that the bluffs in front of the house had not collapsed, after all, Cuicui at first failed to notice that the ferryboat had disappeared.
但再过一阵，她上下搜索不到这东西，无意中回头一看，屋后白塔已不见了。	But as she looked up and down for it, she involuntarily turned around, and the white pagoda behind the house was gone.
一惊非同小可，赶忙向屋后跑去，才知道白塔业已坍倒，大堆砖石极凌乱的摊在那儿。	Startled by the enormity of the loss, she hurried out to the back of the house.  The pagoda had collapsed into a big mass of bricks and stones.
翠翠吓慌得不知所措，只锐声叫她的祖父。	Cuicui was too scared to know what to do next, so she shrilly called out for her grandpa.
祖父不起身，也不答应，就赶回家里去，到得祖父床边摇了祖父许久，祖父还不作声。	When Grandpa did not get up or answer her, she ran into the house and shook him back and forth.  Still he made no sound.
原来这个老年人在雷雨将息时已死去了。	The old man had died as the thunderstorm faded away.
翠翠于是大哭起来。	Cuicui began to wail.
过一阵，有从茶峒过川东跑差事的人，到了溪边，隔溪喊过渡，翠翠正在灶边一面哭着一面烧水预备为死去的祖父抹澡。	Before long, someone going on business from Chadong to East Sichuan arrived at the stream and called out for the ferry. Cuicui was at the stove, crying as she heated water with which to wash the corpse of her grandpa.
那人以为老船夫一家还不醒，急于过河，喊叫不应，就抛掷小石头过溪，打到屋顶上。	The man thought the ferryman's family must be asleep and he was in a hurry to cross.  When his calls went unanswered, he threw a stone across the stream onto the roof of the house.
翠翠鼻涕眼泪成一片的走出来，跑到溪边高崖前站定。	Sniveling and crying, Cuicui ran out and faced the high cliffs by the stream.
「喂，不早了！把船划过来」	"Hey, it's late! Bring the boat over!"
「船跑了」	"The boat has left us!"
「你爷爷做什么事情去了呢？他管船，有责任」	"Where's your grandfather? He's in charge of the boat. It's his responsibility!"
「他管船，管五十年的船－－他死了啊」	"Yes, it's his responsibility, and he did it for fifty years  and now he's dead!"
翠翠一面向隔溪人说着一面大哭起来。	Cuicui blubbered as she spoke to the man on the other side of the stream.
那人知道老船夫死了，得进城去报信，就说：	When he heard that the old ferryman had died, he realized he must return to town and report the news.  He said:
「真死了吗？不要哭吧，我回去通知他们，要他们弄条船带东西来」	"Is he really dead? Don't cry, I'll go back to town and tell people. They'll get you a boat and whatever else you need!"
那人回到茶峒城边时，一见熟人就报告这件事，不多久，全茶峒城里外都知道这个消息了。	When he got back to Chadong, he reported the news to every friend in sight, and soon everyone knew about it, inside the town and out.
河街上船总顺顺，派人找了一只空船，带了副白木匣子，即刻向碧溪岨撑去。	Fleetmaster Shunshun of River Street sent someone to find an empty boat.  Carrying a plain, unpainted coffin, it was dispatched right away, to be poled upriver to Green Creek Hill.
城中杨马兵却同一个老军人，赶到碧溪岨去，砍了几十根大毛竹，用葛藤编作筏子，作为来往过渡的临时渡船。	Horseman Yang and an old soldier hurried over to the site on their own, where they felled several dozen giant bamboos and bound them together with vines to form a raft as a temporary ferryboat.
筏子编好后，撑了那个东西，到翠翠家中那一边岸下，留老兵守竹筏来往渡人，自己跑到翠翠家去看那个死者，眼泪湿莹莹的，摸了一会躺在床上硬僵僵的老友，又赶忙着做些应做的事情。	When the makeshift raft was ready, they poled it to the shore outside Cuicui's house.  The old soldier manned the raft for ferry passengers, while Yang hurried to Cuicui's house to see the deceased.  His eyes brimming over with tears, he stroked his dead friend, now stiff as a board, as he lay in bed. Then he busied himself making the necessary preparations.
到后帮忙的人来了，从大河船上运来棺木也来了，住在城中的老道士，还带了许多法器，一件旧麻布道袍，并提了一只大公鸡，来尽义务办理念经起水诸事，也从筏上渡过来了。	Others came to help out, and the coffin arrived on the boat sent over from the big river.  An old Daoist priest from town ferried across on the raft, bringing his ritual musical instruments, an old sackcloth Daoist robe, and an old rooster, the better to intone scripture, make his waterside pronouncements, and fulfill his other ritual duties.
家中人出出进进，翠翠只坐在灶边矮凳上呜呜的哭着。	People came and went from the house.  Cuicui simply sat on a low stool by the hearth, sobbing.
到了中午，船总顺顺也来了，还跟着一个人扛了一口袋米，一坛酒，一腿猪肉。	Come noon, Fleetmaster Shunshun arrived, too, following a servant who carried a bag of rice, a vat of wine, and a large slab of pork hindquarters.
见了翠翠就说：	He said to Cuicui:
「翠翠，爷爷死了我知道了，老年人是必需死的，不要发愁，一切有我」各方面看看，就回去了。	"Cuicui, I heard about your grandfather's death. Death happens to us all when we get old. Don't you worry, I'll take care of you!" He looked around and went home.
到了下午入了殓，一些帮忙的回的回家去了，晚上便只剩下了那老道士、杨马兵同顺顺家派来的两个年青长年。	In the afternoon, the body was put into the coffin.  People who had come to help began returning home.  By evening, the only ones left were the old Daoist priest, Horseman Yang, and two young workers that Shunshun had sent over from his house.
黄昏以前老道士用红绿纸剪了一些花朵，用黄泥作了一些烛台。	Before dusk fell, the old priest cut out some flower shapes from red and green paper and fashioned candlesticks from yellow mud.
天断黑后，棺木前小桌上点起黄色九品蜡，燃了香，棺木周围也点了小蜡烛，老道士披上那件蓝麻布道服，开始了丧事中绕棺仪式。	When it was dark, a yellow candle was lit on the small table in front of the casket.  There was incense, and other little candles were lit all around the coffin as the old Daoist priest put on his blue hempen gown and began the funeral rite of circling the coffin.
老道士在前拿着小小纸幡引路，孝子第二，马兵殿后，绕着那寂寞棺木慢慢转着圈子。	The old priest went in front, carrying a paper streamer to lead the way, followed by the filially pious daughter and the horseman in the rear, slowly going in a circle around the lonely casket.
两个长年则站在灶边空处，胡乱的打着锣钹。	The two hired men stood in an empty space by the stove, clanging a gong and cymbals to make noise.
老道士一面闭了眼睛走去，一面且唱且哼，安慰亡灵。	The old Daoist walked with his eyes closed, singing and chanting to comfort the spirit of the deceased.
提到关于亡魂所到西方极乐世界花香四季时，老马兵就把木盘里的纸花，向棺木上高高撒去，象征西方极乐世界情形。	When he got to the part about the deceased spirit going to the Western Paradise, where fragrant flowers bloomed all year long, the old horseman raised high a wooden tray of the paper flowers and scattered them over the coffin, to symbolize the bliss of paradise.
到了半夜，事情办完了，放过爆竹，蜡烛也快熄灭了，翠翠泪眼婆娑的，赶忙又到灶边去烧火，为帮忙的人办宵夜。	At midnight, the ceremony came to an end.  They set off firecrackers and the candles nearly burned out.  With tears still streaming down her face, Cuicui hastened to the kitchen to stoke the fire and prepare a midnight meal for those who had assisted.
吃了宵夜，老道士歪到死人床上睡着了。	After the meal, the old priest lay down in the bed of the deceased and slept.
剩下几个人还得照规矩在棺木前守灵，老马兵为大家唱丧堂歌，用个空的量米木升子，当作小鼓，把手剥剥剥的一面敲着一面唱下去－－唱「王祥卧冰」的事情，唱「黄香扇枕」的事情。	The others attended the coffin through the night, as was the custom.  The old horseman sang funeral songs to help the others pass the time, tapping out the rhythm on a wooden grain measuring cup as his drum.  He sang songs about children who were legendary exemplars of filial piety: about Wang Xiang, who lay naked on top of ice to catch a fish for his mean stepmother, and little Huang Xiang, who fanned the pillow of his sick father against the heat and warmed him with his own body to ward off the cold.
翠翠哭了一整天，同时也忙了一整天，到这时已倦极，把头靠在棺前眯着了。	Completely exhausted from crying and working the livelong day, Cuicui rested her head on the front of the coffin and drifted off to sleep, but the two hired hands and the horseman, having eaten and drunk a few cups of wine, were in high spirits.
两长年同马兵吃了宵夜，喝过两杯酒，精神还虎虎的，便轮流把丧堂歌唱下去。	They traded off singing their funeral songs.  Cuicui suddenly reawakened, as if from a dream.
但只一会儿，翠翠又醒了，彷佛梦到什么，惊醒后明白祖父已死，于是又幽幽的哭起来。	She came to the terrible realization that Grandpa was dead, whereupon she took up her anguished weeping again.
「翠翠，翠翠，不要哭啦，人死了哭不回来的！」	"Don't cry, Cuicui, that won't bring him back!"
秃头陈四四接着就说了一个做新嫁娘的人哭泣的笑话，话语中夹杂了三五个粗野字眼儿，因此引起两个长年咕咕的笑了许久。	The old horseman went on to tell a joke about a bride crying on her wedding day, spiced up with a few vulgar expressions that had the two workers howling with laughter.
黄狗在屋外吠着，翠翠开了大门，到外面去站了一下，耳听到各处是虫声，天上月色极好，大星子嵌进透蓝天空里，非常沉静温柔。	The yellow dog barked outside the house.  Cuicui went out and looked up.  The air buzzed with the sound of insects.  The moonlight was grand and bright stars were inlaid in the dark blue sky, creating an atmosphere of calm and serenity.
翠翠想：	Cuicui thought to herself:
「这是真事吗？爷爷当真死了吗？」	"Can it be true? Is Grandfather really dead?"
老马兵原来跟在她的后边，因为他知道女孩子心门儿窄，说不定一炉火闷在灰里，痕迹不露，见祖父去了，自己一切无望，跳崖悬梁，想跟着祖父一块儿去，也说不定！	The old horseman had followed her outside, for he knew that girls did not always show their emotions. A fire might linger under the embers without a trace; with her grandpa gone, and having lost all hope for herself, she might jump off the bluffs or hang herself, following Grandpa in death.  How could they know?
故随时小心监视到翠翠。	Therefore, he kept a constant watch over Cuicui.
老马兵见翠翠痴痴的站着，时间过了许久还不回头，就打着咳叫翠翠说：	Seeing Cuicui standing there in a daze and not turning to him for a long while, the old horseman coughed and said,
「翠翠，露水落了，不冷么？」	"Cuicui, the dew is falling. Aren't you cold?"
「不冷。」	"I don't feel cold."
「天气好得很！」	"It is fine out here!"
「呀－－」一颗大流星使翠翠轻轻的喊了一声。	"Oh!" she exclaimed softly, seeing a big shooting star.
接着南方又是一颗流星划空而下。	Then, in the south, another shooting star coursed down to earth.
对溪有猫头鹰叫。	An owl hooted on the opposite shore.
「翠翠，」老马兵业已同翠翠并排一块块儿站定了，很温和的说，「你进屋里睡去吧，不要胡思乱想！」	"Cuicui," the old horseman said to her softly, having already come up beside her: "Go indoors and sleep a while. Don't let your thoughts run wild!"
翠翠默默的回到祖父棺木前面，坐在地上又呜咽起来。	Cuicui quietly returned to her grandpa's coffin.  She sat on the floor and began sobbing again.
守在屋中两个长年已睡着了。	The two workers standing guard in the house were already fast asleep.
